Current Commentary

Reading Minister Kong's Financial Report 18

— Yan

Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi has compiled a detailed report on the financial situation of the past two years, ending June 30, 1934. It was officially released yesterday. (Full text can be found on the third page of today's newspaper) The content of the report not only provides a general description of the financial situation of the past two years, allowing the people to understand the past national finances, but also outlines the points of emphasis and their implementation in the government's future economic construction, as follows:

(1) Implementing a more effective budget system to control expenditures.

(2) Clearing overdue debts.

(3) Reorganizing the salt tax, implementing a uniform tax rate, abolishing surcharges, improving salt quality, and implementing strict management of production and transportation.

(4) Reorganizing tariff rates to increase tax revenue without affecting industrial products and daily necessities for the general public. As for special export products, reduce or completely eliminate export taxes within a possible range to encourage them.

(5) Continuing to find ways to adjust and reduce provincial and municipal local taxes to achieve a mutually supportive effect with the central tax system.

(6) Encouraging and controlling important domestic industries, such as cotton yarn, cotton cloth, and raw silk.

(7) Stabilizing the currency and unifying subsidiary coins to remove obstacles to industry and commerce.

(8) Improving transportation, especially developing railways and highways.

(9) Aiding agriculture, the foundation of the country, and seeking the development of the rural economy.

Of the above nine items, as far as we know, some have already been implemented successively, and some are being planned and implemented. The facts are clearly verifiable. Judging from the results achieved, such as the clearance of overdue debts in the second item, taking the price of foreign debt in the London market as an example, it has soared to an unprecedented level since the full repayment of the remaining Anglo-French loans and the payment plan for the principal of the Crisp bonds. This is why it enhances our country's external reputation. Secondly, the government's efforts in monetary policy are also obvious. The formulation of restrictions on the exchange of banknotes by provincial or local banks is one aspect of stabilizing the local currency system. The biggest difficulty in our country's currency in the past year has been the threat of the US silver policy. Our financial authorities have been able to take a calm attitude to respond, using silver export taxes and equalization taxes to prevent large-scale silver exports. Regarding the recent repeated increases in silver prices by the United States, the conclusion of a "gentleman's agreement" has eliminated the storm in its invisible form. All of this shows the government's painstaking efforts in stabilizing the currency. What is particularly important is that Minister Kong's report also points out that in today's extremely difficult financial situation, the government still pays attention to economic construction as a way to national rejuvenation. The various achievements listed in transportation and industrial construction are unprecedented in China for decades. Therefore, in Minister Kong's report, his dedication and spirit are clearly visible and should not be regarded as an ordinary political report.

Polish Dictator Piłsudski Passes Away; His Meritorious Service in Restoring the Nation Earns Him Immortal Fame; Kasprzycki Succeeds as Inspector General of the Army 19

Warsaw – General Piłsudski, the pillar of Poland, passed away today at the age of sixty-seven. Piłsudski was the de facto dictator of Poland and one of the most famous figures in modern Europe. Piłsudski had been suffering from abdominal cancer for a long time, but he was still able to meet with British Lord Privy Seal Eden when he visited Warsaw. Afterwards, his condition worsened, so he was unable to meet with French Foreign Minister Laval during his visit. According to officials, Piłsudski's condition was quite serious, and it was not expected that he would pass away. The news of his death spread at 9:30 tonight, shocking the entire country and causing immense grief. Piłsudski's name will endure alongside Mussolini, Kemal, Masaryk, Lenin, and Chang. Piłsudski had great ambitions from a young age, taking the restoration of the country as his responsibility. He dedicated his life to this and died before witnessing Poland break free from its shackles, regain its independence, and join the ranks of European powers. He can die in peace. (Reuters, 12th)

The Circumstances of His Death

Warsaw – General Piłsudski, who fell into a coma last night, passed away at 9:30 after five hours. Professors Wenkebuff of Vienna and Stefanowicz, both renowned doctors, determined that the General had been suffering from stomach cancer, which led to his death. Government ministers and army generals were at his bedside when he passed away. Therefore, there are rumors that the General drafted a political will before his death, but this has not been confirmed. (Havas, 12th)

Warsaw – According to General Piłsudski's doctor, Piłsudski's death was due to nephritis. Piłsudski had been suffering from kidney disease for a long time, and his condition worsened in the past two weeks. His wife and two daughters were by his side when he passed away. His eldest daughter, Wanda, is sixteen years old, and his second daughter, Jadwiga, is fourteen years old. Piłsudski's remains are currently displayed in the Belweder Palace. Government officials gathered here on Monday night, and countless mourning citizens stood solemnly in front of the palace. (National Telegraph, 13th)

National Mourning

Warsaw – Today, the entire country of Poland is mourning Piłsudski. In the early morning, Prime Minister Dr. Kościalkowski led cabinet members to the Belweder Palace to pay their respects to Piłsudski. (Reuters, 13th)

When Piłsudski passed away, government officials were all by his bedside. Piłsudski was still lucid and had no pain. The Ministry of War has been temporarily taken over by General Kasprzycki. At the same time, the government ordered all theaters to suspend performances and radio broadcasts to cancel their programming. (Reuters, 13th)

Emergency Cabinet Meeting

Warsaw – After the death of Minister of Military Affairs General Piłsudski, Prime Minister Colonel Sławek convened the cabinet for an emergency meeting. That evening, a bulletin was issued, urging the public to remain calm, and it was decided to appoint General Rydz-Śmigły (a close confidant of Piłsudski) to succeed the late General as Inspector General of the Army. His vacant post as Minister of Military Affairs will be temporarily held by the current Deputy Minister of the Army, Kasprzycki. (Havas, 12th)

Warsaw – Although important Polish affairs of state were always discussed with Piłsudski before decisions were made, Piłsudski's death will not cause any unrest. The current President of Poland, Mościcki, is an old friend of Piłsudski, and his election also relied on Piłsudski's support. The Polish parliament recently passed a new constitution, granting great power to the President, so that the centralist system created by Piłsudski can be maintained permanently, accommodate all classes, and eliminate party strife. Poland's external position is probably more stable than ever today, due to the following three major reasons: (1) A ten-year agreement with Germany; (2) A non-aggression pact with Soviet Russia; (3) The Franco-Polish alliance is still in effect. (Reuters, 12th)

President Recalls Achievements

Changsha – This morning, the national radio station broadcast a statement signed by President Mościcki, saying that General Piłsudski worked hard to build a strong country and used his intelligence to revive Poland, truly a great figure unprecedented in our history. We must adhere to what he left us, and so on.

Condolence Telegram from German Head of State 20

(Berlin) – The sudden death of Polish national hero General Piłsudski has caused great grief throughout Germany. Head of State Hitler, on behalf of the German government and himself, sent a telegram to the Polish President, saying, "We are deeply saddened to hear of the death of General Piłsudski. On behalf of our government, we extend our condolences to Your Excellency the President. Poland has lost a founding hero with the General's passing, and the entire German nation joins the people of your country in mourning the death of this great hero. The General's cooperation with Germany has not only greatly benefited the relations between Germany and Poland, but has also contributed to peace in Europe." (National Telegraph, 13th)

(Berlin) – Political circles in Berlin were greatly shocked by the news of General Piłsudski's death, but they generally believe that it will not affect relations between Germany and Poland, as they believe that the ten-year agreement between the two countries depends on the nature of events and that the rise and fall of individual politicians will not make much difference. (Reuters, 11th)

A Will Discovered; Brain Donated for Scientific Dissection; Heart Buried in Family Cemetery with Deceased Mother 21

Warsaw – The government newspaper stated that General Piłsudski expressed in his will that his brain should be donated for dissection to show Piłsudski's respect for science. The newspaper added that the main points of the will are as follows:

(1) The General's heart should be transported to his birthplace, the city of Vilnius. (2) His mother's remains should be reburied in Vilnius, and his heart should be placed at his mother's feet. (3) His remains should be buried in the Wawel Cathedral in Krakow, where Polish kings throughout the ages are buried. (National Telegraph, 13th)

Piłsudski's remains will be transported to the Wawel Royal Castle in Krakow Province, where former Polish kings and national heroes are buried. Piłsudski's will stipulated that his brain be donated to Polish university students for scientific exploration, and that his heart be buried with his mother's ashes in the Piłsudski family cemetery in Vilnius. (Reuters, 13th)

It is reported that General Piłsudski will probably be buried in Krakow on May 18. (Havas, 13th)

A Brief History of Piłsudski 22

General Piłsudski was born on December 5, 1867, in Zułów, near Vilnius. Piłsudski's family was wealthy. In 1863, because his family participated in demonstrations against the Tsar, most of the family's assets were confiscated by the Russian authorities. Therefore, Piłsudski grew up in a pro-Russian atmosphere. In 1874, Piłsudski's estate was destroyed by fire, and the family moved to Vilnius. At that time, the family property was declining, so life was very simple. Piłsudski studied at the Vilnius High School, where he often violated school rules. He was reprimanded by Russian teachers for speaking Polish in the school square. In 1885, he completed his preparatory work and entered Kharkov University to study medicine. Piłsudski was arrested and imprisoned twice for participating in revolutionary movements. At the age of twenty, he was arrested for plotting to assassinate Tsar Alexander III and exiled to Siberia for five years. From then on, his determination to resist Russia became stronger. At the age of thirty-two, he was imprisoned in the Warsaw Citadel for more than a year. Before long, he escaped from prison and fled to Austria. From then on, he acted more cautiously, and he expected that Austria and Russia would eventually meet on the battlefield. Therefore, he secretly organized Polish battle teams in Austria. In 1905, when Russia and Japan fought in Manchuria, Piłsudski went to Tokyo to join the war, intending to start an uprising behind the Russian army line to disturb it, but the Japanese authorities did not allow it, and his plan failed. In 1914, Piłsudski's opportunity suddenly came. After Piłsudski was released from exile in Siberia, he instilled the idea of ​​raising troops to resist Russia and restore Polish independence in the minds of his compatriots. He fought tirelessly for decades. Piłsudski, in view of the failures of 1830 and 1863, not only sought to resist the powerful Russia, but also worked to eliminate the self-debasement of his compatriots, because those people were afraid of Russia's power and advocated reconciliation with the Russian government. Piłsudski was confident that his cause would eventually succeed, so even if his entire family opposed him, he would not be discouraged. He was also resourceful and good at predicting things. In 1914, Piłsudski predicted that the world war would break out. The Polish Riflemen team he organized in Austria was used to join the Russian army in combat, hoping to make contributions to restore Poland's freedom. Piłsudski personally led the First Brigade of the Polish Foreign Legion, which then

Piłsudski's Portrait

Page 6

became the backbone of the Polish army. In June 1917, Polish detachments fighting in the Russian, German, and Austrian armies all recognized Piłsudski as their leader. On the night of July 20, 1917, Piłsudski was detained by German officers in the Magdeburg fortress for refusing to swear allegiance to the Central Powers. A year earlier, at the request of the German Supreme Commander, the Central Powers announced their intention to restore Poland's freedom. Piłsudski was summoned from the countryside to organize a provisional government in Warsaw, in which Piłsudski also held a seat. Before long, he had a disagreement with German officers. Piłsudski was imprisoned in the Magdeburg fortress. It was not until the Central Powers failed in November 1918 that he was released. On the 10th of that month, Piłsudski formally entered Warsaw and became a national hero. Two days later, he was elected as the provisional President of Poland. On the 2nd of February 1919, the Polish Republic's parliament formally declared Piłsudski as the head of state. At that time, the constitution had not yet been established, so he was not elected according to law. In 1921, the new constitution was promulgated, and the presidential election was held according to law the following year. In November 1920, the entire Polish army publicly elected General Piłsudski as the first general. In that year, Piłsudski formally visited France and Romania, and the people of both capitals praised him as the savior of Poland. In 1923, Piłsudski resigned from the position of head of state and retired to the countryside to write his autobiography. In 1926, Piłsudski was convinced that the country was gradually showing signs of pre-war chaos and was in danger of bankruptcy, so on May 12, he led several detachments of troops into Warsaw. After three days of street fighting, he overthrew President Wojciechowski and the Witos cabinet. Thereupon, the people all elected Piłsudski to resume the presidency, but Piłsudski strongly refused and elected his old friend Mościcki, who had conspired with him in the revolution, to replace him. Since 1926, Piłsudski has always served as the Inspector General of the Army and Minister of Defense, except for holding the post of Prime Minister twice (once from 1926 to 1928, and once in 1930). Piłsudski married Maria Juszkiewicz in 1894. His wife also participated in the revolution and was once imprisoned. They had two daughters. Piłsudski was the de facto dictator of Poland in his later years. Often, when he held state affairs meetings, if his daughter happened to arrive, he would stop the meeting and listen to his daughter tell about her school affairs. Piłsudski was quick to handle affairs. In November 1918, he arrived in Warsaw from Magdeburg at 8 pm. After meeting with 32 representatives of various political parties, he worked day and night and quickly restored order and prevented the country from falling into chaos. Piłsudski often walked to the Ministry of Defense every day and worked until 3 or 4 pm, then went to bed until 9 am the next morning. Whenever he thought about important matters, he would walk around the room. This habit was probably acquired in Russian prisons, and he smoked countless cigarettes, all specially made for Piłsudski, so they were called "General Cigarettes." Whenever Piłsudski made an important decision, he would first rest for half an hour to recuperate. When he played cards, he always used 13 as his lucky number. (Reuters, 13th)

Thirty Years Ago, He Fled to Japan; Hirota Kōki Once Served as His Interpreter 23

(Tokyo) – The sudden death of General Piłsudski, the de facto dictator of Poland, was reported by all newspapers here, which recounted his life and achievements and sent condolences to Poland. Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota said in an interview with journalists that he met General Piłsudski thirty years ago during the Russo-Japanese War, when Piłsudski was a political prisoner living in Japan. At that time, he was a university student and served as General Piłsudski's interpreter. (Reuters, 13th)

(Tokyo) – General Piłsudski, the Polish dictator who died yesterday, was a Russian revolutionary member during the Russo-Japanese War and stayed in Japan for half a year. Foreign Minister Hirota spoke today as follows: At that time, I was a student and was entrusted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to serve as an interpreter. General Piłsudski and three others were introduced by General Akashi to visit Yamae Enjiro of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and meet with General Fukushima, requesting to continue the war and destroy the Romanov family. One day, he said he wanted to try Japanese food, so he ate raw carp in a restaurant and even ate the eyes of the raw carp. If it were someone else, he would definitely spit it out, but Piłsudski was always strong and swallowed it with whiskey. He was truly an outstanding figure at that time. (Den Tsushin, 13th)

Italy and France Reach Sky Agreement: Negotiations in Progress 31

(Berlin) According to a Rome dispatch in the Berliner Tageblatt, negotiations between French Aviation Minister Denain and the Italian military authorities are underway. The goal of both parties is to conclude a Franco-Italian sky agreement of a military alliance nature. According to reliable sources, the main points are as follows:

(1) The contracting states shall notify each other of the quantity and effectiveness of their air forces at any time. (2) If the air force of one of the contracting states is attacked by a thirteenth country, it must immediately come to the aid of the other party. (3) Once a war breaks out, for the sake of unified command of the air forces of both sides, another agreement should be made to stipulate alternating command or, depending on the actual situation during the war, to be placed under the command of one party. (4) The areas in which the air forces provide mutual assistance should also be determined.

Because of the provisions of these practical clauses, the newspaper believes that the effect of this sky agreement is more practical than the Franco-Russian agreement. At the same time, this kind of mutual assistance is entirely automatic, so once it is launched, the land and naval forces of the two countries will inevitably be mobilized at the same time. Although the governments of the two countries will still have to use the Anglo-French declaration of London as a talisman on the surface, its nature will inevitably be very different from the spirit of the London Declaration. (National Telegraph, 12th)

Shanghai Concession: Factory Inspection Negotiations; Inspection Office Writes to Director of National Labor Bureau for Assistance 37

(Nanjing) Regarding the Shanghai Concession factory inspection negotiation case, it is rumored that since the closing of the 18th International Labor Conference, Cheng Haifeng, director of the Chinese branch, has contacted the concession authorities as a third party. However, due to the unclear attitude of the concession authorities, the negotiations are still shelved. The Inspection Office has no choice but to first strive for the promotion of factory inspections in various provinces and cities, and request the Ministry to instruct Director Li to appeal to this conference and conduct serious negotiations with representatives of various countries, and directly write to Director of the International Labor Bureau Butler, requesting assistance in the Shanghai Concession factory inspection negotiations, so as to resolve them in the shortest possible time. The original letter is translated as follows: "Mr. Director Butler, after the previous dispatch of Mr. Bourne and Mr. Bedson from your bureau to China to provide assistance, our country's factory inspection has benefited greatly. This office was established in August of the 22nd year and has formulated implementation plans and procedures in accordance with various relevant labor laws and regulations, and has taken the establishment of a factory inspection foundation" and "promoting factory inspections in various countries" as the policy guidelines. So far, 19 provinces and cities have implemented it according to law. Among these 19 provinces and cities, those that have completed the first phase of work in accordance with the "Factory Inspection Implementation Procedures" formulated by this office include Weihaiwei, Hankou, Beiping, the urban area of Shanghai, and five places in Henan Province. Most of the remaining provinces and cities will be completed in June of this year, which is gratifying. Factory inspections in various provinces and cities have made considerable progress in recent years (see the 23rd China Factory Inspection Annual Report). If this continues, our country's factory inspection can achieve satisfactory results. However, the failure to resolve the Shanghai Concession factory inspection negotiations is not only the most unfortunate event for the future of factory inspection in our country in Shanghai, but also deeply regrettable. In order to maintain the integrity of China's factory inspection administration, at the 18th International Labor Conference, Mr. Li Pingheng, the former director of our country's government delegation, gave a detailed account of the negotiation process. At that time, I was assured that I would communicate with the relevant countries to solve it as soon as possible. After the director of your branch, Cheng Haifeng, tried his best to mediate in a private capacity, the Shanghai Concession authorities had an unclear attitude, which caused this negotiation to remain in a deadlock. Now that this International Labor Conference is about to open, our country's representatives should still make statements in accordance with their original intentions, and I hope that your bureau director will give practical assistance so that the Shanghai Concession factory inspection negotiations can be resolved in a short period of time." (Special Dispatch, 13th)

Yan Xishan Explains the Nature of Property Securities: Shanxi Province Is Inconvenient to Implement Alone 40

(Taiyuan) After Shanxi Province began to implement the Ten-Year Construction Plan, Yan Xishan instructed several commissioners to hold meetings to study the matter of issuing property securities. This measure has also aroused the attention and questioning of public opinion circles across the country, and the meeting has repeatedly explained to dispel doubts. Recently, according to the final results of the research, Yan made a specific answer when a student asked him during a speech at the Shanxi Local Administrative Personnel Training Institute, saying, "Property securities can be implemented independently by the province in nature, but the province is inconvenient to implement independently in terms of political power, because property securities must be granted the status of legal currency by the central government in accordance with laws and regulations before they can be used as a medium of transaction and a measure of value. Since the province does not have this power, it is inconvenient for the province to implement it independently." According to this statement, this type of securities may only be used as research data and the issuance may be suspended. (Special Dispatch, 13th)

Acceptance of the Yellow River Project Is Completed; Fu Rulin and Others Pass Through Xuzhou and Return to Nanjing 51

According to reports, the rapid closure of the dam this time was not due to local efforts alone, but due to (1) unified powers and responsibilities for work and disaster relief: Ren Guantai and Ren Jiugu of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission; (2) uninterrupted central government funding; (3) assistance from Henan and Hebei provinces in materials and ships; (4) the convenience of the Ministry of Railways ordering the Longhai and Beining Railways to allocate trains to transport stones; (5) the efforts of the staff at all stages of the project. Therefore, Guantai completed the closure ahead of schedule, and Jiugu closed the four breaches, and three water protections were built, namely the Taihang and Zinc Dams. In the future, the dike project can be considered to be in good condition. If there are major floods, it is still difficult to predict. It is planned to return to Nanjing and request the central government to establish a special Yellow River agency to control the water conservancy authorities of the provinces along the river, and to plant trees within 100 meters of the riverbanks to regulate the climate, prevent sand, and protect the dikes. After the Yellow River dam closure, it will be temporarily handed over to the Hebei and Henan provinces for safekeeping. Li Yizhi and Kong Xiangrong remained in Bianliang to supervise. Statistics on Criminals Falsely Arrested and Detained in the 22nd Year 54

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Interior, statistics on criminals falsely arrested and detained by public security bureaus in major cities, public security bureaus in counties under Jiangsu and 17 other provinces in the 22nd year have now been completed. A. The number of criminals in major cities is the highest in Shanghai with more than 17,000, followed by Beijing with more than 15,000, Nanjing with more than 8,000, Guangzhou with more than 7,000, Wuhan with more than 4,000, and the capital of Gansu Province with only more than 90. The most common crime was opium-related offenses with more than 22,000 people, followed by theft with more than 17,000 people, injury with more than 11,000 people, internal rebellion with more than 1,200 people, counterfeiting weights and measures with the least at 2 people, abortion with 3 people, and foreign aggression with 5 people. B. The number of criminals in Jiangsu and 17 other provinces is the highest in Hebei with more than 19,000 people, followed by Shanxi with more than 17,000 people, Zhejiang with more than 15,000 people, and Qinghai with only 40 people. The most common crime was opium-related offenses with more than 28,000 people, followed by gambling with more than 18,000 people, theft with more than 10,000 people, foreign aggression with only 14 people, neglect of duty with 72 people, and internal rebellion with 88 people. (Central News Agency, 13th)

They departed last Saturday and are expected to take one month. Director Li Kezhen of each group will continue to go to Anyang, Henan for archaeological excavations. Norwegian General Munthe Passes Away 61

(Beiping) General Munthe, who had resided in Beiping for many years, passed away in Beiping this morning. It is said that he died of heart failure at the age of 70. Munthe was Norwegian and came to China in 1887 to work in the customs. In 1896, during the Sino-Japanese War, he was appointed as the discipline instructor of the Beiyang Model Army and later became Yuan Shikai's adjutant. He was a collector of Chinese art and sold a portion of his collection to the Los Angeles Museum of Art in the United States several years ago, but he still kept many of the fine art pieces given to him by the Qing Dynasty and Yuan Shikai, unwilling to sell them. His wife, who has written several books on Chinese history, is currently in England. (Reuters, 13th)

International Commercial Telegram - Special Commercial Report from Reuters, May 13th - 75

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today's price is 142 shillings and 6.5 pence, down 9.5 pence.

London Silver Market: The market was slightly unstable this morning, but prices rose. Spot prices rose by 5 to 33.5 pence, and futures rose by 1.875 to 33.625 pence. India and China bought, while speculators sold. The closing sentiment was stable.

Mount Isa Silver: Although London silver prices rose today, the opening price of Mount Isa fell. The July price was 75.40, down 10 pounds.

Exchange Rates

British Pound vs. US Dollar: The London foreign exchange market was very quiet this morning. European purchases of British pounds caused the exchange rate to rise, but the price fell back as purchases decreased. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was 4.86615, up 0.00375 from the closing rate on Saturday. It rose 0.00812 within the first hour to 4.874375. In the next forty minutes, purchases surged, causing the price to jump 0.020625 to 4.895. It then fell slightly, dropping 0.00125 at noon, 0.0025 at 1 PM, and another 0.0005 at 2 PM to 4.88625. One US dollar is equivalent to 4 shillings and 1.117 pence.

British Pound vs. French Franc: The opening price was 7x francs 93, up 11 points from the closing price on Saturday. It rose 4 points within the first hour, and the price surged in the next forty minutes to 74 francs 31. However, it fell back 16 points at 2 PM to 74 francs 15.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market was quiet today, and prices were slightly lower than before. Futures prices fell due to foreign sales.

British Cotton: Liverpool cotton market prices also fell today. The July price was 6.48 at 1 PM, down 8 points.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened with a slight price decrease due to favorable weather reports. The morning market trended downward. The trend of miscellaneous grains was similar to that of wheat.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market fell today due to unfavorable news from the US. The July price was 5 shillings and 5.625 pence at 1 PM, down 0.875.

Rubber

London: The opening was stable today, and the morning was calm. The July and September prices were 5.875 pence at noon, up 0.0625 from Saturday's close.

New York: Prices rose by 12 to 14 points due to improved prospects for the automobile industry. Sentiment is gradually improving due to the belief that the Rubber Restriction Committee will eventually raise prices, and it is expected that statistical positions will improve in the short term.

Securities

New York: Prices at the opening today were equal to the closing prices on Saturday, and later there was a slight upward trend. Traders tended to be bullish. The labor strike in the automobile industry is showing signs of resolution, so traders are quite excited. The general public expects that Secretary of the Treasury Morgenthau's speech tonight on the dollar will aim to gauge the public's attitude towards the movement to stabilize the currency. Although there is currently a trend in the market to wait for Morgenthau's speech, the market is also quite active. Railroad stocks had the highest increase, and oil stocks were also stable. Under the Harsh Taxes of the Puppet Organization, Harbin Businesses Are Closing Down One After Another; More Than Fifty Companies Closed Down in Mid-April 98

Harbin Correspondence: Harbin's commerce has been in a state of decline for a long time. According to merchants, the reason is that the business is shouldering a heavy burden due to the harsh business taxes imposed by the puppet organization. In addition, the countryside is exhausted and purchasing power is weak. Various trade associations and chambers of commerce have repeatedly sent representatives to appeal to the puppet organization, but the puppet authorities have been whitewashing and delaying commercial relief due to competitive relations between Japan and the puppet organization, so that Japanese businesses can flourish. As a result, Chinese businesses that cannot sustain themselves are closing down daily. According to reliable surveys, in April alone, more than 50 companies under the jurisdiction of the Daowai Chamber of Commerce closed down. Among these 50-odd companies, Fuzengsheng, Qingfaxiang, and Erliang Rice Shops, and Gonghelong Bank are all old merchants in Harbin for many years. Not only do they have strong capital, but they also have close ties with various merchants. From this, it can be seen that the wounds of major merchants are all over their bodies, and the dangerous phenomenon will be fully exposed when the silver root is unusually tight in May. However, although 229 companies were opened in mid-April, these were all unemployed people who are suffering from the difficulty of finding a job due to the depression in the market and oversupply of labor. In order to make a living, they pooled extremely small amounts of capital to temporarily engage in business to meet their current needs. The weakness of their funds can be imagined, and the results will still be closure. (Northeast News Agency)

Financial Report for the Republic of China for the Fiscal Years 21 and 22 99

(I) Introduction

The central financial report for years before the 21st year was compiled and submitted by former Minister Song. In October of the 22nd year, Xiangxi was ordered to succeed as the head of the Ministry of Finance. At that time, the 21st year had just ended, and the materials for various reports had not yet been collected. Due to the transition, there was not enough time to complete them. In January of the 23rd year, the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee was held, and in December, the Fifth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee was held. Xiangxi had successively prepared financial reports and submitted them for review. Now, a comprehensive compilation of the previous two reports has been made to form a detailed report for the 21st and 22nd fiscal years, along with a presentation of the general financial situation since the beginning of the 23rd year, as follows:

The first half of the 21st year coincided with the aftermath of the January 28th Incident. The national crisis was severe, and government officials worked diligently and cautiously, striving to economize on military and administrative expenses. At the same time, the people's patriotic fervor was also extremely strong. The government was able to revise the domestic debt repayment method, reduce the burden on the national treasury, and barely balance income and expenditure. By the spring and summer of the 22nd year, the suppression of bandits in Jiangxi Province was in full swing, and the situation in Yuyu and Rehe became critical, with martial law declared in Pingjin, resulting in huge expenditures for military provisions. As the military situation stabilized somewhat, there was a need for substantial relief funds for the war zones. After autumn, the Yellow River suffered a massive inundation, and the rebellion in Fujian Province followed. The raising of relief funds and the payment of military salaries were almost overwhelming. Therefore, the second half of the 21st year and the first half of the 22nd year were truly the most difficult periods for the national finances within the two fiscal years.

Fiscal revenue has always relied heavily on customs duties. Since the 20th year, the world economic panic has affected our country, with falling prices and rising silver prices affecting international trade. Customs revenue has therefore been reduced. In addition, the total loss of customs and salt taxes in the four northeastern provinces, as well as the need to find alternative ways to compensate for the portion of foreign debt originally secured by the tax revenues of those provinces, has further increased the burden of government debt.

Fortunately, the adoption of the gold unit for customs duties, the increase in import tax rates, and the improvement of financial and tax administration have prevented tax revenue from decreasing significantly. However, the increase in revenue from the above measures is far less than the previous losses.

Based on the above reasons, the government's financial deficit still had to be covered by borrowing. The amount borrowed in the 21st year was 86 million yuan, and the amount borrowed in the 22nd year was 147 million yuan. However, at the same time, debt was repaid, approximately 100 million yuan in the 21st year and approximately 115 million yuan in the 22nd year. In comparison, the amount borrowed was roughly offset by the amount repaid.

Looking back to the beginning of the 22nd year, the government could still make do with selling old bonds and borrowing temporary funds to cover the financial shortfall. However, by October of the 22nd year, as the need became more urgent and resources were exhausted, 100 million yuan in customs treasury bonds for the 22nd year were issued to facilitate turnover.

When Xiangxi took office, the finances were in a state of extreme exhaustion. Overall, the monthly deficit was often as high as 15 to 16 million yuan. At a time when military operations were in full swing and disaster victims were awaiting relief, it was impossible to reduce large expenditures and risk undermining the foundation. Therefore, efforts were made to reorganize tax revenues to increase the annual income. The tax rates on tobacco, cigarettes, matches, and cement were appropriately increased, and the customs duties on wheat flour, kerosene, gasoline, and other imported goods were appropriately revised. Import taxes on foreign rice and wheat were also implemented. At the same time, reforms were planned to increase revenue. However, the deficit was too large, and the increase in tax revenue could not be achieved overnight. Moreover, when the turmoil had just subsided, the financial situation was extremely tight, and stability in the market urgently needed to be addressed. In addition, the Central Bank had excessive thermal funds and should also find ways to repay them. Therefore, 100 million yuan in customs treasury bonds for the 23rd year were issued to repay advances and stabilize the financial situation.

Examining the total annual expenditure, military expenditure still accounted for the largest share, amounting to 321,000,000 yuan in the 21st year and 373,000,000 yuan in the 22nd year. However, the reason for the increase in these figures is that the scope of military expenditure included in the income and expenditure reports for this year was broader. For example, expenditures between various ministries and commissions that fell within the scope of military expenditure were mostly reported by this department during this period, and military expenditures from previous years that were gradually transferred during these two years were also included in the report. The amount of these supplementary items was 59 million yuan in the 21st year and 46 million yuan in the 22nd year. In addition, a portion of construction costs, such as the construction of roads in the bandit suppression areas and relief for rural villages, was also paid from the military expenditure item. From a practical perspective, the military expenditure for the two years has not exceeded previous years. This is because the military authorities have been considerate of the people's difficulties and have striven for frugality, enduring hardships and refraining from making excessive demands. Therefore, despite the successive events of suppressing rebellions and combating communism, the increase in military expenditure has been limited. Currently, the bandits' nests in Jiangxi Province have been destroyed and cleared, and the suppression of the part that fled to Sichuan and Guizhou is also progressing smoothly. If the bandit scourge can be eradicated at an early date, the reduction of military expenditure is a matter of course.

The rise and fall of the public debt market is enough to see the credit of the government and the safety of society. In the past two years, the prices of domestic and foreign debts have risen. From December 15th of the 21st year to February 25th of the 24th year, the 1913 Rehabilitation Loan bond in the London market has risen from 77 to 99.75. The 1898 loan bond has risen from 97.5 to 105, and the 1908 British-French loan bond has risen from 73 to 99.75. Although the situation of all domestic debts has been through two issues of treasury bonds, the market price has increased. This is because the government has reorganized old debts and carefully preserved the public debt fund, which has made the people at home and abroad increasingly trust the government.

However, during this period, the world economy was in turmoil, and our country could not be immune to the contraction of currency, the fall of prices, and the decline of industry and commerce, which all had a major impact on finances. In addition, foreign purchasing power was extremely weak, and various countries in the United Kingdom and the United States implemented national currency policies. The values of currencies such as the British pound, Japanese yen, and US dollar have depreciated, resulting in an increasing gold ratio of the Chinese silver dollar, and international trade has become more depressed.

In the autumn of the 23rd year, the domestic financial situation was tight. At that time, the United States Congress passed the Silver Purchase Act, and our country's domestic silver flowed out in a steady stream, and the number of exports was the largest in history. In order to protect domestic silver reserves and curb the rise in the price of national currency, the government had no choice but to increase the silver export tax and implement a balancing tax to regulate the situation. In recent months, silver exports have gradually decreased, and the market has stabilized. However, currency and finance are still serious problems in our country. The government is making every effort to plan various measures to rectify the financial situation, rescue the market, encourage production, and promote domestic goods in order to overcome the difficulties. The world is in the midst of turbulent waves, and we cannot but be terrified.

(II) Income and Expenditure

All expenditures in the 21st year were based on the budget for the 20th year. The general budget for the 22nd year was reviewed and compiled by the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, but the actual income and expenditure figures were based on the books of the Ministry of Finance. The following table lists the materials compiled based on the various pastoral expenditure reports received within the two years, and does not include all income and expenditure items that should be received and paid. Therefore, the figures in the table contain income and expenditure that belongs to previous years but was reported in the current year, and income and expenditure that was not reported in the current year will also be listed in the next year's table.

In addition, the Ministry had previously proposed a method for the central government agencies to manage income and expenditure, which should be handled uniformly by the national treasury, and submitted it for approval and implementation. Since its implementation in January of the 22nd year, a portion of the income and expenditure of the central government agencies has been included in the following table, which is more detailed than the income and expenditure table of previous years.

(III) Customs Duties

The level of customs duties is closely related to the livelihood of the people, and the government must take this into account. In May of the 22nd year, the import tariff regulations were revised, and the tax rates on textiles, paper, and fish and seafood products were slightly increased. In the winter of the same year, import taxes on rice and wheat were levied, and the import tax rate on wheat flour was increased to protect the interests of domestic farmers. In order to increase tax revenue, the tax rates on kerosene and gasoline were also slightly increased. By the end of the 22nd year, all import tariff regulations were revised again after considering the gains and losses. These new tariff regulations were implemented in July of the 23rd year.

The disaster relief surtax was originally set at 10% of the import and export tariff regulations. On August 1st of the 21st year, it was changed to 5%. In order to compensate for the annual budget, an additional 5% customs surtax was levied. The implementation period was initially set for one year and has now been extended to the end of June of the 24th year.

On April 6th of the 22nd year, an export tax of 2.25% ad valorem was levied on silver ingots, silver bars, and silver blocks. However, exports of factory bars and silver coins minted by the Central Mint were exempted. The 2.25% export tax rate is equal to the minting fee charged by the Central Mint for minting factory bars and silver coins, and is intended to use the tax rate to balance the national silver price. In October of the 23rd year, due to excessive outflow of silver, an export tax of 7.75% was levied on factory bars and silver coins from the 15th, and an export tax of 10% was levied on large silver bars and other silver categories. It was also stipulated that if the difference between the London silver price converted to the Shanghai exchange rate and the exchange rate determined on that day was insufficient to pay the above export tax, a balancing tax would be levied based on the insufficient amount. The details of the above two points are detailed in the Currency section.

The government originally planned to abolish all customs duties that impede domestic trade, such as re-import taxes, sub-port taxes, and inland regular customs duties. Since the 20th year, these have been gradually abolished. The re-export tax was intended to be abolished at the same time as the above taxes, but due to the sudden reduction of a large amount of revenue in finance, it was necessary to first find a way to compensate for it, so it was temporarily retained. It is still intended to be resolutely abolished in the shortest possible time. In the past year, the government has separately reduced or exempted various export and re-export taxes for goods transported abroad and domestically. For example, export taxes on peanuts, peanut kernels, peanut oil, eggs, and egg products were successively reduced in the 22nd and 23rd years. As for grains such as rice and wheat, which were previously subject to re-export taxes and prohibited from being exported, the ban was lifted from January of the 22nd year due to low prices and stagnant sales, and both export and re-export taxes were exempted. In June of the 23rd year, all export tariff regulations were revised again, mostly using lower tax rates, and more than 60 types were completely exempted. This year, it is planned to continue to appropriately reduce and exempt the majority. All of these are deeply rooted in the fact that export trade has plummeted in recent years, and rural villages in the country are on the verge of bankruptcy. Therefore, no effort has been spared to sacrifice huge amounts of tax revenue in order to save them.

With higher tax rates, tax evasion is even more difficult to avoid. Therefore, customs equipment has also been carefully reorganized to ensure strict prevention. Items such as adding patrol ships, increasing patrol teams, and establishing wireless communications have all been expanded. At the same time, the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations were promulgated, and customs posts were added at various land, sea, and air entry points to curb the source of smuggling. Although the trend of smuggling has not been completely suppressed in the past two years, the results of anti-smuggling have indeed been significant. According to customs investigations, some items that were previously mostly smuggled in are now taxed according to regulations.

After the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan in the spring of the 22nd year, the customs taels used for export and re-export taxes were also abolished and replaced with silver standard currency. The weights and measures used for customs duties ad valorem were also adopted in February of the 23rd year using the new standard system.

The total amount of customs revenue (including import regular tax, export regular tax, re-import tax, inland sub-port tax, and ship tax, but excluding the disaster relief surtax and customs surtax) from the 1st year of the Republic of China to the 23rd year is listed in the table below.

The decline in customs revenue since the 20th year is mostly due to the decrease in the total value of imported goods. The total value of imports and exports in the 22nd year, excluding the four northeastern provinces, was only two-thirds of that in the 20th year. The total value of imports and exports in the 23rd year fell by 20% compared to the 22nd year. In addition, the prevalence of smuggling in South China and North China has also had some impact on the reduction of customs duties.

Another reason for the reduction in customs duties is the loss of customs duties in the four northeastern provinces. The customs revenue of the four provinces, including Dalian Customs, was nearly 40 million yuan according to the 20th year. This tax revenue has been completely lost, and the portion originally designated to guarantee foreign debt has also been lost, resulting in the government increasing its burden in addition to reducing revenue.

Page 10

(IV) Salt Administration

During this period, the amount of salt tax revenue has increased significantly, and the administration of the salt administration has also striven to improve. The main points of its reforms are listed as follows:

(1) Merger of Institutions: The salt administration institutions in our country inherited the system of past dynasties, and the organization varied depending on local conditions. In order to concentrate power and save expenses, the government has appropriately merged them. Currently, the salt administration in various places has been mostly merged into the inspectorate for concurrent management.

(2) Elimination of Illegal Levies: Officials in various districts demanded illegal levies, which had been a long-standing practice, especially in the Yangtze River areas. Efforts have been made to eliminate them, so that the cost of salt merchants can be reduced.

(3) Reorganization of Tax Rates: The tax rates in various districts vary, and the burden is not evenly distributed, making smuggling more prevalent. In order to equalize taxes, the government implemented a preliminary reorganization of the salt-producing areas in July of the 21st year, and in October of the 22nd year, the sales areas were appropriately increased or decreased for the second reorganization. On January 1st of the 23rd year, an order was issued that the total amount of regular and additional taxes on salt should be limited to 10 yuan if it was between 10 yuan and 13 yuan, and an additional tax of 3 cents for foreign debt and 1 cent for salt field construction was added. For those below 10 yuan, improvements will be made gradually in the future after observing local conditions.

(4) Adoption of Standard Weights and Measures: On January 1st of the 23rd year, the Ministry ordered the adoption of the new metric system (one market dan equals 50 kilograms—110.23 pounds) to replace the local units that vary according to local customs.

(5) Construction of Warehouses and Fields: Salt fields are built in the producing areas for storage, and roads and ports are built to facilitate transportation, so that the salt produced can be quickly reached the storage area and it is easy to combat smuggling. This construction project has been gradually completed in the Huaibei and Changlu salt areas, and is now gradually being promoted in Shandong, Huainan, Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong and other regions.

(6) Construction of Storage Yards: It is planned to gradually build warehouses in the central salt sales areas, so that the salt from various places can be stored in them, so that the collection, transportation, sales, and collection of salt taxes can be facilitated.

(7) Reorganization of Tax Police: For the reorganization of tax police, the first step is to eliminate the old and weak, recruit elite troops, rectify discipline, and establish a tax police officer training school. Since its implementation, it has achieved good results. The salt tax in various districts across the country, except for the three northeastern provinces and the Koubei district, which are affected by special factors, is remitted on schedule for the amortization of foreign debt principal and interest funds. The salt tax allocated for the Hubei-Guangdong Railway loan even exceeds the amount that should be amortized according to the original contract and is sufficient to pay the full interest on the loan each year.

8th

Chen Jitang Detains Zhu Yuan - Zhu Zhuowen Executed in Zhongshan County - Yuan Dai Escorted to Guangzhou Awaiting Punishment 100

Guangzhou Dispatch: Zhu Zhuowen, a veteran member of the Kuomintang, was arrested in Zhongshan County by Liang Gongfu, the head of the Second Regiment of the Military Education Division, acting under the orders of Chen Jitang. The following night, Zhu was executed on the spot. The details are as follows:

Earlier, Chen Jitang accused Zhu Zhuowen and Yuan Dai, an advisor to the First Group Army Headquarters, of organizing a militia and smuggling military equipment in Zhongshan County, plotting wrongdoing. Last month, he ordered Liang Gongfu's troops to station themselves in the area for strict surveillance and secretly instructed them to arrest Zhu and Yuan if necessary and send them to the province for interrogation. On the first of this month, he specially dispatched the Zhongkai warship to Shiqi to provide support and ordered Liang to immediately arrest Zhu and Yuan. After receiving the order, Liang ordered the officers and soldiers of the regiment to strengthen defenses day and night while dispatching dozens of capable secret agents to guard key locations in the town. He also devised a plan to lure Zhu into submission. On the sixth, Liang sent out invitations, inviting Zhu and others to a banquet at Zhang Tianji Restaurant in Shiqi at 6:00 PM that afternoon. At the same time, he ordered Deputy Regiment Commander Zhang to lead a company of soldiers, equipped with hand grenades and light machine guns, to set out from their garrison at the South Gate. They advanced along the streets in a "hornet formation", encircling the area. Upon reaching their destination, they ordered the soldiers to fix bayonets and stand guard on the main roads, as if facing a major enemy. At that time, all pedestrians and vehicles on the roads and streets of the town were temporarily forbidden from passing, and several light machine guns were set up at each intersection. The residents were bewildered and fled in panic, creating an atmosphere of fear and anxiety. Simultaneously, the shops in the town, thinking that a battle was about to break out, successively closed their gates. The prosperous commercial town was suddenly silent, like a ghost market. Around 6:00 PM, Zhu, accompanied by his attendant Dong Yuan, arrived as agreed, unaware of the trap. During the banquet, Wu Zhiqiang, the finance director during Liang Hongguang's tenure as county magistrate, Li Shaoqin, the chief of public security, Li Cheng, a provincial councilor (representing Zhongshan County), Zheng Zhongchu, the head of the Fourth District of the county, and Wu Ding and other local elders, totaling eight people, were also present. After several rounds of drinks, as the eighth dish was served, Liang Gongfu ordered the guards waiting at the door to go upstairs, raise their guns, and stand ready. He also ordered everyone at the table to stand up and raise their hands. The guards then detained Zhu. Seeing this, Zhu's attendant Dong Yuan tried to draw a pistol to resist, but he was discovered by the guards, who disarmed him and escorted Zhu to the regiment's office. Liang then showed Zhu Chen Jitang's secret order. Zhu remained silent. Subsequently, Li Shaoqin, Wu Zhiqiang, Li Cheng, former officials of the county, and local elders went to the Second Regiment headquarters to petition Liang Gongfu, requesting the release of Zhu Zhuowen. Liang replied that he was acting under the orders of his superiors and could not comply with their request. They returned empty-handed. After Zhu Zhuowen was arrested, Liang Gongfu sent a company of armed soldiers to the Yongle Hotel on Changdi Street in the town, surrounding it completely. Deputy Regiment Commander Zhang, along with the company commander and platoon leaders, prepared to resist arrest with gunfire. However, Yuan Dai, realizing the overwhelming odds, feared a massacre if they opened fire. He forbade the guards from firing and decided to wait for a resolution. Seeing that Yuan and his men did not resist, the officers and soldiers disarmed all the guards. Yuan Dai was then shackled and, along with three other people (names unknown), was taken to the Zhongkai warship and escorted to Guangzhou. Half an hour later, a large number of soldiers were dispatched to the second floor of the Yongle Hotel for a thorough search, apparently to capture remaining accomplices. However, Yuan's remaining associates had already fled upon hearing the news and could not be found.

After Liang Gongfu captured Zhu and Yuan, he posted a public notice around 11:00 PM that evening, stating: "By order of the Commander-in-Chief of the First Group Army: It has been reliably reported that Zhu Zhuowen, Director of the Construction Bureau of Zhongshan County, and Yuan Dai, Advisor to the Headquarters, are smuggling military equipment and organizing a militia in Zhongshan, plotting wrongdoing. The Regiment Commander is ordered to arrest them and send them to the Headquarters for disposition. Upon receipt of this order, it was found that the two rebels dared to smuggle military equipment and organize a militia in Zhongshan, endangering the local area, which is extremely unsupportable. The rebels were captured on the sixth and will be sent to the province for trial today. Since the ringleaders have been apprehended, the followers should be spared. All merchants and residents are hereby notified not to be alarmed. This notice."

After Yuan Dai was escorted to Guangzhou, he was interrogated by Li Jingxi, the chief of the military law department appointed by Chen Jitang, and then sent to the headquarters of the military police for detention. Zhu Zhuowen remained in Zhongshan County under the guard of Liang's regiment. Upon receiving the report, Chen Jitang sent He Luo, the chief of the public security bureau, to Zhongshan County on the seventh to interrogate Zhu, accusing him of ordering over ten thousand small, circular badges from a jewelry store on Hui'ai Road in Guangzhou. The first batch of the ordered badges were being investigated to determine their origin. Zhu denied any connection with the badges. However, at 3:00 AM that evening, Liang Gongfu, acting on Chen Jitang's orders, executed Zhu.

It is reported that after Zhu Zhuowen was detained, Zhu's confidants rushed to the province to seek his release. Zou Lu, a standing committee member of the Southwest Political Affairs Council, believed that Zhu had followed Sun Yat-sen in the revolution for decades and had contributed significantly to the party and the country. He sent a letter to Chen Jitang, requesting his release. Chen reportedly replied to Zou, stating that he had approved the request to transfer Zhu to the province for interrogation. Therefore, those who spoke for Zhu believed that if Chen allowed Zhu to be transferred to the province, there might be room for maneuver in the case. At the same time, influential figures also sent telegrams to Chen Jitang, asking him to consider Zhu's past contributions and grant his release. The telegrams arrived like snowflakes. However, Chen Jitang had already made up his mind to kill Zhu and specifically ordered Liang's regiment not to transfer Zhu to the province, precisely to avoid pleas from various parties. (Eighth)

Wuxi: Natives of Jingjiang Request Severe Punishment for Suppressing Public Opinion 101

Li Yinfang, the magistrate of Jingjiang County, arrested Liu Jianfan, the editor of the Jingjiang Daily, because the newspaper published a short story titled "Injection," which he believed alluded to an affair between the magistrate and Ms. Zou Jinyong, the director of the obstetrics department of the smoking cessation hospital. Liu was detained in the local prison, subjected to illegal torture, and sentenced to one year and eight months of imprisonment. The newspaper was also forcibly ordered to cease publication. The newspaper has telegraphed various sectors for unanimous support. It is learned that Liu Zhengmin and 30 other fellow townsmen of Jingjiang traveling together, believe that the aforementioned report did not contain transgressive language, and that the magistrate had illegally arrested the reporter and ordered the paper to cease publication, abusing his authority. Such trampling on human rights and suppressing public opinion is extremely unlawful. Yesterday, they jointly telegraphed Chen Guofu, chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Yu Jingtang, director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and the Provincial Party Headquarters, requesting that they be severely punished according to the law to uphold public opinion and protect human rights.

Nantong: Continuing Training for Township Heads 102

Zheng Yitong, the administrative inspector of the Nantong District, stated that two sessions of the training class for township heads of the six counties under the district, including Tong, Ru, Chong, Hai, Jing, and Qi, have already been held. He has now found that there are still people who are required to receive training according to the regulations and will continue to open the third session. Classes will begin on the 20th, with each person required to pay 30 yuan. If they continue to refuse under false pretenses, the county government will enforce it.

Changshu: Home of County Party Committee Member Robbed 103

The home of Wu Zhongying, an executive committee member of the County Party Committee, located in Dongjing Town, Third District, was robbed by more than 20 bandits around 3:00 AM the night before. They traveled for an hour to reach Wu's home and began the robbery. They bound Wu's uncle, Xiaotao, and other village officials with bedding before plundering the house. As a result, more than 50 silver dollars were stolen. They then went to the lower room to find the family of Wu's father. Wu's father was lucky enough to escape early and was not harmed, but all important valuables were looted. At the same time, the home of farmer Dai Shijin in Xiangjing, about seven or eight miles away, was also robbed. Dai was stabbed twice and seriously injured in the waist. Reports have been filed with the Public Security Bureau for arrest.

Jiashan: Citywide Strike Calmed 104

The strike by merchants and residents in the urban and rural areas of this county due to the county government's moving of puppets late at night has been reported in various newspapers, but none have been detailed. It has been learned that the county government issued a seal on all temples in the city on the 3rd of this month and announced martial law on the 5th, with a complete police cordon and armed defense. However, there were still rumors of a temple fair on the 11th. The county government secretly ordered police officers, patrol teams, and the security corps to hire several large boats in the middle of the night on the 11th and transport all 13 puppets from the city to the Yasheng Temple. In addition to sealing the temple doors, police were stationed to guard it. The next morning, residents outside the East Gate heard the news and convened an emergency meeting. Starting from the Jiashan Oil Factory near the Sunjiaqiao bridge, thousands of people went door-to-door to spread the word of a strike. Within an hour, all shops in the city had completely closed. The Public Security Bureau, upon hearing the news, sent the section chief and inspectors to dissuade the crowd together with the head of the security corps, but to no avail. The county government immediately convened an emergency meeting to discuss countermeasures. Police officers with live ammunition were stationed in front of the county government, the Public Security Bureau, and the headquarters of the security corps. The streets were crowded with pedestrians, and the atmosphere was extremely tense. Shen Jiren, a standing committee member of the County Party Committee, feared that the situation would escalate and decided to resolve it peacefully. He persuaded both sides not to push for a break. The heads of each community then ordered each village to guide the people into the city and return the idols one by one. They agreed to allow each temple to operate, as a condition for mediation. Therefore, all shops in the city have resumed business today. However, whether or not the temple fair will be held is still undecided.

Director Feng Rui of the Guangdong Department of Agriculture and Forestry Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss Investment with the Central and Other Four Banks 107

The Shenshi News Agency reports that Feng Rui, director of the Department of Agriculture and Forestry of Guangdong Province, arrived in Shanghai at 10:30 AM yesterday aboard the President McKinley to establish a water conservancy and reclamation company. The Four Banks Invest in the Water Conservancy Company

In order to revitalize the rural areas and promote development, Guangdong Province plans to establish a water conservancy and reclamation company. My purpose in coming here is to discuss the distribution of the funds in detail and sign a contract.

Proceeding with Loan for Guangdong's Sugar Industry

The water conservancy company will have nine directors, five from the banking sector and four from the government. The directors appointed by the government will be approved by the banking sector. I will also take this opportunity to discuss the sugar industry with the Shanghai banking community. I plan to visit the leaders of the four banks tomorrow (today) and go to Nanjing within a few days to make a presentation to the central government, he said.

Mayor Wu Advocates Combining Education and Entertainment - Plans to Establish Shanghai City Day and Create City Song - Reports Significance at Municipal Government Memorial Week Yesterday - Promoting New Movement to Advance Municipal Social Construction 108

The Central News Agency reports that in order to promote the New Life Movement and advance municipal social construction, Mayor Wu has advocated establishing a day as the municipal festival and creating a Shanghai city song. He reported the significance of the proposed Shanghai City Day and the creation of a Shanghai city song at the Municipal Government Memorial Week yesterday. His words were quite earnest. The original text is as follows: Fellow comrades, the purpose of my report today is to suggest to the citizens of Shanghai that we establish a day as Shanghai City Day and create a Shanghai city song. On the one hand, I want to explain my ideas, and on the other hand, I want to solicit the opinions of all citizens. The direction of the Shanghai Municipal Government's efforts this year has been determined as social construction. Therefore, this year is the Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Construction Year. On the one hand, we want all municipal government employees to work in this direction, and on the other hand, we want to awaken all citizens of Shanghai to support the municipal government and cooperate with the municipal government to complete the various undertakings planned for our Social Construction Year. We must know that social construction is different from other types of construction. Other types of construction mostly focus on material aspects, while social construction must also focus on spiritual aspects. All municipal government employees and citizens of Shanghai should not overlook this important point in the course of our efforts in municipal social construction. On the negative side, we must transform customs, and on the positive side, we must build our spirit. In the process of national revolution, in the construction of a new China, and in the progress of the Chinese national revival movement, we must find ways to eliminate all obstacles, both tangible and intangible, that currently hinder the national revolution, hinder the construction of a new China, and hinder the revival of the Chinese nation. This work is our most urgent task at present. The so-called intangible obstacles are more powerful than tangible obstacles. For example, customs have a historical background and have been passed down for thousands of years. They have a great controlling power over the psychology of the general public. However, many customs are good, and many violate the spirit of the times. We must of course preserve good customs. We must not only preserve them but also promote and develop them. However, we must find ways to improve or even eliminate those customs that violate the spirit of the times and hinder social progress. This is an important work that we must strive to fight for when the old and new clash. Because each era has its own spirit and needs, many of the customs passed down in China for thousands of years are no longer in line with the spirit and needs of the current era. These customs that violate the spirit and needs of the times are intangible obstacles that hinder social progress and the construction of a new China. We should improve or eliminate them. Everyone must recognize that now is an era of scientific omnipotence, now is an era of human power over nature. We must exert human power to survive, which is in line with the modern spirit. However, many of our customs are contrary to the modern spirit. The most obvious examples are seeking divine guidance, temple fairs, burning incense, and dispensing free meals to the gods, etc., all kinds of unconscious actions. For example, a few weeks ago, it was reported that the people of Luodian in Jiading County dispensed free meals to the gods, praying for divine blessings and disaster relief. A few weeks ago, a temple fair was held in Jiaxing. The government prohibited it, resulting in a strike. Also, a few weeks ago, temple fairs were held in Pudong and Jiangwan. Although the situation this year was slightly better than in previous years due to the city government's efforts to prohibit them in advance, these unconscious actions and customs that violate the spirit of the times are still prevalent and still have great social potential. We must use political power to prohibit them and lead the people to take a very rational path that is in line with the spirit of the times. The construction movement of our new China has been underway for more than 50 years, and the national revolution led by our party's founder has also been underway for more than 50 years. However, to this day, most people still follow the old forces and live in the old thinking. If we do not destroy these old forces and old thinking, what methods can we use to build a new China and revive the Chinese nation? Chiang Kai-shek, in view of this, deeply knows that revolution must first revolutionize the heart, and change must first change customs. Therefore, he wants to promote the New Life Movement, because the way of life is most closely related to social progress. A bad way of life will of course only create a bad society. This is a certain truth. If the way of life cannot be improved, then our society cannot be improved. Therefore, Chiang Kai-shek wants to promote the New Life Movement and instruct local governments, local party departments, national civil servants, and national Kuomintang comrades to use political power and persuasive methods to promote the New Life Movement. If we want the national revolution to succeed thoroughly, we must first transform the lives of the people throughout the country. If we want to transform the lives of the people, we must first eliminate all bad customs that violate the spirit of the times. Therefore, the most important task of our New Life Movement is to transform customs. However, to transform the Chinese society, which is deeply rooted and has the deepest historical teachings, in addition to using political power, we must also use social education methods to guide the situation. And the best way to guide the situation is to combine education and entertainment. Therefore, we want the Shanghai Municipal Government to advocate that a day be set as Shanghai City Day, so that millions of people in the city, regardless of social status, men and women, old and young, rich and poor, can all enjoy a day of common joy and happiness every year, which is the so-called public entertainment. We must have various meanings and messages incorporated into the forms of entertainment on this day, such as encouraging agriculture, encouraging learning, encouraging industry, encouraging commerce, and promoting diligence and thrift, so that citizens throughout the city can stimulate their passionate emotions, lively spirits, and noble meanings and sound thinking in the midst of the excitement of Shanghai City Day, thereby creating a new atmosphere in the city. At the same time, we also want to create a Shanghai city song. This song should be very popular so that everyone in the city can sing it. The content should also carry the consciousness of encouraging agriculture, encouraging industry, encouraging learning, encouraging commerce, and promoting diligence and thrift, in order to eliminate the decadent music of the city and cultivate the healthy temperament of citizens. In short, we want to gradually transform those customs that violate the spirit of the times through this joyful festival and this song. At the same time, we also want to take this opportunity to create a new custom to inspire the noble aspirations and lively spirits of the citizens throughout the city. This is an important work in the social construction of the city. This method of advocating local festivals is not an innovation. All countries and regions have local festivals, the so-called Carnival. Various regions of our country also have their own festivals. I am only improving them according to the spirit of the times and the needs of the environment. When we talk about Shanghai in Shanghai, we must preserve and promote the good customs of Shanghai. However, we must also find ways to improve all customs in Shanghai that violate the spirit of the times. We see that the citizens of Shanghai today simply do not have a day of common joy and happiness in the 365 days of the year. In the past, during the lunar new year, everyone, regardless of social status, men and women, old and young, rich and poor, and even those in debt, was happy. Now the lunar calendar has been abolished and the solar calendar has been adopted. However, the solar calendar has not yet been popularized. Only a few people are following the solar calendar, and most people do not know how to use it. Therefore, the kind of excitement and joyful emotions during the solar new year is of course not possible. And the weekly holiday is still a new system. Except for national administrative agencies and a few banks and factories that implement the weekly holiday system, other places have not yet popularized it. Even if it is popularized, it still cannot make the public happy together. Even on National Day, October 10th, people do not seem very happy. We see how happy and joyful the people of other countries are on their National Days. How widespread is it? But the people of our country are still indifferent to National Day and of course there is nothing happy to say. One reason is that the time is too short, and there have been various changes in between. Another reason is that we are now in a time of national crisis and seem to have no intention of celebrating National Day. Therefore, when we talk about Shanghai in Shanghai, we really cannot find a day that can make all the citizens of Shanghai happy together, and we cannot find a day for conscious entertainment. No wonder most citizens throughout the city frown every day and are troubled and annoyed. On the one hand, people who are lazy by nature are indulging in improper entertainment every day or even at every moment. Under such circumstances, what methods can we use to awaken the passionate emotions of the citizens? And what methods can we use to inspire the lively spirits of the citizens? If this continues, those strange phenomena and customs such as temple fairs and burning incense can only exist every day and become more widespread every day. This will not only hinder the progress of the construction of a new China and the revival of the Chinese nation, but the people's morale will also decline day by day, to the point where it is beyond remedy in the future. The danger ahead is truly unimaginable. Therefore, based on the principles of the New Life Movement, the principle of revolutionizing the heart before revolutionizing the government, and the principle of transforming customs, we must preserve and promote the good customs of Shanghai. As for all the customs that violate the spirit of the times, we must distinguish between the priorities and transform them step by step. The method of transformation is to "combine education and entertainment" and lead the citizens throughout the city to engage in common entertainment. Set a Shanghai City Day so that all citizens, regardless of gender, age, wealth, or poverty, can come together to enjoy entertainment on this day. During the entertainment, promote the spirit of encouraging agriculture, encouraging industry, encouraging learning, encouraging commerce, as well as thrift and reading, so that entertainment becomes meaningful, popular, socialized, and educational. At the same time, we must also create a Shanghai city song for all citizens to sing, so that the decadent music that permeates the city can be changed, the enthusiastic emotions of the citizens throughout the city can be awakened, and the depressed and troubled society can be transformed into a lively and happy society. A city full of such passionate and happy emotions can prosper and develop. By extension, if a nation is full of such passionate and happy emotions, it can transform the conservative and decadent national character, develop social activity, and increase national sympathy. In this way, there will naturally be hope for revival, and so on.
