Polish Embassy Flew Half-Mast Yesterday in Mourning of Piłsudski: Founding Hero of Poland Dies in Warsaw; Memorial Service Scheduled 110

Marshal Józef Piłsudski, the founding hero of Poland and Minister of Military Affairs, passed away at 8:45 PM on the 12th (previous day) at Belvedere Palace in Warsaw due to illness, at the age of 68. Poland has lost its sole leader, a truly significant loss. The Polish Consulate in this city received the telegram officially yesterday morning at 11:00 AM and immediately flew the flag at half-mast in silent mourning. Polish Minister Wędtowski and Polish expatriates in Shanghai will hold a memorial service and prayer service. The original telegram was in French, translated as follows: General Józef Piłsudski, the first marshal of Poland, passed away due to illness at Belvedere Palace in Warsaw on the 12th of this month at 8:45 PM. General Piłsudski had been ill for several months. Professors Wenka Bell and Stevens diagnosed the general's illness as cancer of the liver and stomach. Famous military and civilian doctors worked together to treat him, but without success. By May 11th, the illness became critical, with internal bleeding causing the heart to weaken, ultimately leading to his demise. Piłsudski was born on December 5, 1867, and was 68 years old. He studied medicine at a Russian university. At that time, Poland suffered the pain of being partitioned. Piłsudski dedicated himself to revolutionary work, fighting against the Tsarist Russian government. He was arrested repeatedly but never ceased his revolutionary work. He was once exiled to Siberia for five years. During the European War, Piłsudski secretly organized volunteer armies in Poland to resist Russia. More and more people joined, and the momentum grew, fighting for Poland's independence and winning repeated victories. In 1917, Piłsudski was imprisoned by the German government in a military prison. The following year, the Great War ended, and Piłsudski was freed. Poland finally achieved independence through Piłsudski's efforts. An interim government was established, and he was elected as its leader. When the formal constitution was completed, although he was elected as the first president, he firmly declined and retired to the post of Minister of Military Affairs, where he remained until now. In 1920, he repelled the Russian army invading Poland, further enhancing his reputation. He was undoubtedly a national hero.

Shanghai Municipal Council Court Agreement Expires in March Next Year; Legal Circles Believe Revisions Are Necessary; Judicial Yuan Also Pays Close Attention 111

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Council Court Agreement, which extended its validity for three years from April 1, 1933, will expire at the end of March 1936. Legal circles in this city believe that the agreement must be revised after its expiration, and the judicial authorities are also paying close attention to this matter. The Ministry of Justice is now organizing a Legal Rights Research Committee to discuss the recovery of consular jurisdiction. According to the Central News Agency reporter's inquiries with legal circles, the situation is as follows:

Expires in March Next Year

The Shanghai Municipal Council Agreement was signed in Nanjing on February 17, 1930, by Xu Mo, representative of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Dias, Chargé d'Affaires of Brazil in China, Jacob, Minister of the United States in China, Hurley, Minister of Great Britain in China, Gronwald, Chargé d'Affaires of Norway in China, and Herlongmen, Chargé d'Affaires of the Netherlands in China. It came into effect on April 1 of the same year. According to Article 10 of the agreement, the validity period is three years. After it expired at the end of March 1933, it was extended for another two years with the consent of both parties. It is expected to expire at the end of March next year.

Must Be Revised

Legal circles in this city believe that the provisions of the agreement must be revised after this term expires. There are ten articles and eight attachments in the agreement, and many points should be revised. The most notable are: (1) the issue of jurisdiction; (2) the issue of police dispatch. The prosecutor of the Shanghai Municipal Council Court is limited by the provisions of the agreement, and has very little jurisdiction. All public prosecution matters are handled by the police. The selection of judicial police is not directly assigned by the president of the court, but the police recommend candidates, and then the president of the court assigns them.

Judicial Yuan Pays Close Attention

Judicial circles in this city generally believe that the organization of the Shanghai Municipal Council Court is different from that of courts in other regions. Therefore, after the expiration of the agreement, it must be revised to be the same as courts in other regions. It is also known that the Ministry of Justice is paying close attention to this matter and has begun to organize a Legal Rights Research Committee, which will be established soon. The issue of recovering consular jurisdiction will be studied by the committee.

Some Foreigners' Wild Ideas

Recently, some foreigners in this city have suggested establishing an international arbitration court to handle foreign-related litigation. The judicial circles expressed indignation at this. At a time when China is actively recovering consular jurisdiction, there should be no such attempts to undermine the integrity of China's legal rights. It is also known that this suggestion is the wild idea of a few foreigners and will definitely not be realized.

Nie Kaiyi Returns to Shanghai Yesterday; China National Aviation Corporation's Chongqing-Kunming Line Successfully Completes Trial Flight 112

According to the Guowen News Agency, the China National Aviation Corporation's giant Ford aircraft, piloted by pilot Lyle Sonn and co-pilot Wang Guanyue, flew to Chongqing as early as March 25 to conduct a trial flight to Kunming. I have returned to Shanghai and reported the trial flight process to the company authorities and the Ministry of Transportation, requesting them to consider the situation, set the schedule, and announce the official opening.

The pain in this is beyond description by pen and ink. The above points are brief contributions. In short, the national product industry in our country is in a dangerous situation today and should earnestly unite, first seek a way to save ourselves, and then plan to resist foreign aggression, so as to fulfill our industrial responsibility to save the country. May we rise together and plan for it. Zhang Guoquan, general manager of China Enterprise Company, said in his speech that our country's industry has never had an organizational foundation from the beginning. After January 28, the social economy was extremely panic. In addition, foreign goods were overproduced and inflation occurred. Due to the increase in silver prices, a large number of commodities were exported at low exchange rates, and dumping was carried out. Our national product factories did not dare to ask the government for assistance, nor did they rely on any economic power. They all emerged to fight automatically. Now, Mr. Wu Zhihao is enthusiastic about saving the country, advocating industry, adopting simple methods, concentrating organizations, and organizing a joint business office of various factories in order to promote the sales of national products and achieve the hope of industrial salvation. All our national product factories unanimously agree, and it is heard that Mr. Wu's Ningbo Industrial Bank undertakes national product warehouses, national product markets, and national product mobile pawnshops, which can provide our industrial circles with genuine cooperation and assist in production, which is even more gratifying.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance Announces the Names of Foreigners Who Have Not Paid Land Value Tax 121

Foreign nationals from certain countries have not paid land value tax on their perpetual lease land in the city. It is reported that the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance has issued a notice to these foreign nationals, as follows: It is found that the city's collection of provisional land value tax is in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the central government. All land within the area designated for the collection of provisional land value tax in the city, whether it is perpetual lease land or land with land certificates, must pay taxes in accordance with the regulations. The tax period is divided into two installments each year. The first installment started on August 1, 1933, and has now reached the fourth installment. The estimated land value is based on the assessment of the Estimation Committee organized in accordance with the regulations. The committee consists of nine members, including four famous figures from the business community, who are very familiar with the real estate situation. Mr. Gui Yanfang, chairman of the Chinese Real Estate Association, is one of them. Therefore, the estimated land value is very fair. Compared with the actual value, it is reduced by an average of about 55%, and the tax rate is set at 6 per thousand per year, which is also a light tax. Moreover, there is no discrimination based on national boundaries, and it is collected uniformly. Moreover, the landowners in the city enjoy great benefits on their land, but there are no taxes on these benefits. Landowners should enthusiastically pay the small amount of land value tax currently collected in the city to fulfill their obligations. It is found that the household's registered number is , the land value tax for the second installment of the perpetual lease land for 1933, 1934, and 1935 is a total of ocean yuan, jiao, fen. The Bureau has previously issued tax notices with serial numbers such as Di, Tian, Yuan, and Huang to the household, but no payment has been made, which is not in accordance with the regulations. It is the duty of the Bureau to notify and urge the tax defaulters to pay the tax, and it has also notified the Land Bureau that when perpetual lease land or land with land certificates that has not paid land value tax is transferred, no transfer will be allowed to restrict it. Moreover, Articles 8 of the Provisional Regulations on the Collection of Land Value Tax and Article 14 of the Implementing Rules stipulate that "If the taxpayer fails to pay the tax in accordance with the regulations within the prescribed time limit, he may be summoned to recover the tax arrears and shall be charged annual interest on the tax arrears, and may also extract the income from the land and its fixtures based on the number of years of arrears, and may submit it to the municipal government for approval to auction the land and its fixtures to offset the tax arrears, as well as the annual interest to be charged." This is a point that taxpayers should pay special attention to. This notice is hereby given, and it is hoped that you will check and pay the tax as soon as possible to avoid being punished in accordance with the regulations. To the owners of the land, Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance.

Observatory Report: Low-Pressure Wind Has Entered the Sea of Japan; Green Huangpu River Water Due to Prolonged Drought 125

The low-pressure wind that originated within our country's borders affected this city when it entered the sea the day before yesterday morning. Therefore, the city experienced a fierce wind attack at around 3 AM on that day. However, according to the observatory report, the typhoon situation is still the most significant. The wind has now entered the Sea of Japan, located between 135 degrees east longitude and 40 degrees north latitude. According to the person in charge of the observatory, speaking to a reporter from the Dagong Society, "Depression" should be translated as "low-pressure wind" because low pressure is also a type of hurricane. Otherwise, outsiders may not understand. A hurricane that originates on land is called a low-pressure wind in astronomy. Therefore, hurricanes and low-pressure winds are both strong winds, but their situations are completely opposite. Hurricanes originate at sea and travel from west to east, while low-pressure winds originate on land and travel from east to west. The one that affected this city the other day was a low-pressure wind. As for the green color of the Huangpu River water recently, it is due to the prolonged drought and has nothing to do with the rise and fall of tides.

Commercial Press Compiles and Prints Series Integration for Sale Pre-Orders – Compiling the Great Achievement of Series – Broadening the Dissemination of Ancient Books 128

The compilation of series in our country began with Yu Fengsun's "Confucianism Awakening" in the Song Dynasty, followed by Zuo Yuxi's "Hundred Rivers Learning Sea." During the Ming and Qing Dynasties, there were more and more refined compilations. All surviving classics, lost histories, good customs, benevolent governance, admirable deeds, and strange anecdotes were examined and briefly described. However, there were thousands of volumes published from the Song Dynasty to the Qing Dynasty, and among them, the names and realities did not match in five or six out of ten cases. Deletions, revisions, and trivial matters were even more common. If one did not choose carefully, purchasing many volumes would waste money, and reading them indiscriminately would waste energy. Since resuming business, the Commercial Press has successively published the "First Collection of Rare Treasures from the Complete Library of the Four Branches of Literature," the "Supplement to the Four Branches of Literature," and "Forty Kinds of the Wanwei Secret Collection" in terms of promoting national essence and circulating ancient books. Now, with the same purpose, it is further organizing the old series in our country, selecting the best of the good books from the series collected by the library over the years, eliminating repetitions, organizing the format, and naming it "The First Compilation of Series Integration." The selection criteria are based on practicality and rarity, the former to meet needs and the latter to circulate orphan copies. Roughly divided into three categories: ordinary series, specialized series, and local series. Each category is divided into several sections. All books are uniformly punctuated and printed on high-quality Daolin paper. It is divided into 4,000 volumes. The cause and general catalog were published in various newspapers at home and abroad in March of this year. Pre-orders have started on the 1st of this month. The original engraved value of the one hundred selected series is over 10,000 gold. The library's organized typesetting pre-order price is 460 yuan if paid in one lump sum this month, 500 yuan in June, and 540 yuan in July. There are also separate payment methods for the convenience of buyers. Sample copies and pre-order brochures are available for solicitation. There is also a thick catalog, which contains abstracts and classification explanations of the one hundred series, priced at two cents per copy. The essence of domestic series, what libraries and collectors spend huge sums to seek but cannot obtain or is not easy to obtain, can now be obtained at one-twentieth of the price of the original book, and everyone can obtain it. Isn't this a happy event? Contemporary sages believe that organizing national studies is a necessary path to revitalize the nation. The library's compilation and printing of this series integration meets the needs of the times, and those who cherish predecessors and respect local sages can also use this to glimpse their writings and theories, which is beneficial to both academic research and cultural training.

Pudong Fellow Villagers Association Petitions the Municipal Government to Dredge Agricultural Rivers to Facilitate Farmland Irrigation and Transportation – Water Conservancy Agency Under Review by Economic Council 131

The Pudong Fellow Villagers Association believes that the main rivers in Pudong have been neglected for many years, and the accumulated silt is increasing day by day, affecting both farmland irrigation and ship transportation. Therefore, it has specially petitioned the Municipal Government to be in charge and dredge the rivers. Furthermore, the association's Standing Committee member Du Yong and others suggested establishing a Huangpu Water Conservancy Agency. The National Economic Council has ordered the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission to formulate measures for review and handling. A reporter from the Dagong Society has investigated and reported the following details.

Petition to the Municipal Government to Dredge Agricultural Rivers: Petition to devise ways to dredge the main rivers in Pudong to benefit farmland and transportation. We earnestly request that the competent authorities review and handle the matter. We believe that water conservancy is related to the national economy and people's livelihood and should be valued by the administration. Therefore, the National Economic Council has listed it as a major task, and the government has long had the "Shanghai Municipal River Regulations" and a river system table. The rivers in the East River section listed in the system table as second-class main rivers are the Dajiangpu and Zhaojiagou in the Gaolu districts, the Bailianjing in the Tangyang districts, the Gaoqiao Port in the Gaochang districts, the Yangjing Port in the Yangjing district, and the Yangsi Port in the Yangsi district. The rivers listed as first-class tributaries are the Yangjiabang in Gaoqiao, the Xiantangbang in Gaoxing district, the Duqianpei and Lujiugou in the Gaolu districts, the Majiabang and Zhuangjiagou in the Luyang districts, and the Huacaozhongfenjing in the Yangtang districts. The above rivers are used for farmland irrigation and ship transportation, and they are no less than the water lifeline of the entire Pudong. Most of the rivers have been accumulating silt for many years and urgently need to be dredged. Last year, the weather was arid and dry, and the farmland suffered considerable losses. It is imperative to make amends before it is too late. The association held its fourth general meeting of members on February 17th of this year and the 35th board meeting on March 14th. After detailed discussion, it was unanimously decided that the administrative authorities should be requested to conduct surveys and construct in stages. According to reports from members, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works and the Chuansha County Government consulted on dredging Zhaojiagou the year before last. The Chuansha territory was completed in the spring of the 23rd year, but the Shanghai territory has not yet started construction, and the smooth flow of the Shanghai territory has caused serious damage due to the tide and siltation. Furthermore, in the autumn and winter of last year, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works guided the organization of the Yangjing District River Dredging Committee to raise funds for dredging various rivers such as Yangjing Port, but it was unable to proceed due to lack of funds, and it will become a pipe dream. Now that your government is planning to relieve rural businesses, it seems that focusing on water conservancy should be the top priority. In addition to the above-mentioned Zhaojiagou Yangjing Port, which have been planned, please instruct the Bureau of Public Works to list them as the most important projects and handle them in accordance with the first item in Article 2 of the River Dredging Regulations. Other main and tributary rivers in Pudong should also be planned at the same time or carried out in stages, and we hope that they will be completed in the near future. All reasons for requesting the dredging of the main rivers in Pudong to benefit farmland and transportation are hereby presented for review and approval, and for forwarding to the Bureau of Public Works for responsible handling. We await instructions with deep public gratitude. Respectfully submitted to Shanghai Municipal Government Mayor Wu.

Water Conservancy Agency Under Review by Economic Council: The Pudong Fellow Villagers Association believes that the Huangpu River waterway is shallow and narrow. It specially established a National Economic Council to organize and reorganize the Huangpu River waterway agency, and transferred the existing funds of the Junpu Bureau to the reorganization agency, so as to be solely responsible for guarding it. The association has received a reply from the Economic Council stating: Upon receiving your request, we believe that the Huangpu River waterway is gradually becoming shallow and narrow, and we intend to organize and reorganize the agency in accordance with the Yangtze River method, and attach four brief descriptions to the council. After reviewing this case, the case was previously sent by the Water Conservancy Office of this Council to the Jiangsu Provincial Government with the same reason. The original documents were copied and attached by this Council, and the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission was ordered to review and reply to the case. It should wait for the reply to arrive at the council before reviewing and handling it. This response is for the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association for your information.

Qimei Road: Low-Income Housing to Be Built Soon – Designs Have Been Finalized, Totaling 242 Units 132

The Shanghai Municipal Government plans to build low-income housing for the welfare of the common people. Yesterday, Liu Hongdian of the Municipal Expansion Center Construction Committee told a reporter from the Shenshi Society that the Municipal Government has decided to first build the low-income housing near Qimei Road. The designs were finalized by the Low-Income Welfare Undertakings Committee last Friday. The low-income housing in that area is divided into two types, A and B. There are 200 units of type A housing, equipped with a living room, bedroom (i.e., mezzanine), kitchen, and toilet, connected by five rooms. There are 42 units of type B housing, equipped with a living room, kitchen, toilet, and other facilities, connected by two rooms. For the sake of air circulation, both types A and B housing face south, and the alleys are on one side. All housing is also equipped with a low-income elementary school, 20 men's bathrooms (shower), 15 women's bathrooms (shower), an auditorium, a clinic, a consumer cooperative, a tea room, a sports field, a public toilet, a laundry room, and other facilities, which are very thoughtful and complete. The construction cost for both types A and B housing and all attached facilities is approximately 120,000 yuan. The rent for each unit of type A housing is approximately 3 yuan, and the rent for each unit of type B housing is approximately 3.5 to 4 yuan. Type B housing has a bedroom, while type A housing only has a mezzanine, which is more convenient, so the rent is more expensive. Each unit of both types A and B housing can accommodate four to six people. Now that the designs have been finalized, bidding will be solicited for construction soon, and construction can begin in the shortest period of time. As for the Tanziwan housing, the designs have not yet been finalized, so the construction period will be slower.

Child Kidnapped on Rue Lemaire, French Concession, Last Night – Li Guanlin's Son, Jinxiang, Kidnapped – Four or Five Bandits Escaped Completely 133

On the extreme west Rue Lemaire in the French Concession, there is a rural area called Houlijiazhai. Most of the residents have the surname Li. Among them is Li Guanlin, a local, 36 years old, whose ancestors have lived here for generations. He has several acres of land, which he cultivates himself. He married Ms. Shen in his early years, who is now 32 years old. They have a son named Jinxiang, who is only four years old. The family is harmonious and happy. Moreover, because the Li couple is diligent and thrifty, they have some savings. Recently, they hired workers to build more than ten bungalows on the ancestral property in the area and rented them out. Unexpectedly, this attracted the attention of bandits. At around 9 PM last night, four or five short-dressed bandits wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, each holding a pistol, broke into Li's house. Li's wife, Ms. Shen, was holding Jinxiang and sitting idly in the living room. When the bandits entered the house, they first snatched Li's son, Jinxiang, from Ms. Shen's arms. Ms. Shen was terrified and screamed. A bandit fired a shot into the sky to warn against resistance. Ms. Shen was unable to resist, and because the area was unusually remote, no one came to help, allowing the bandits to calmly kidnap Li's son. Afterwards, Li reported to the French Concession police. The captain immediately dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to search for the bandits, but they had already escaped without a trace. The police are now making every effort to investigate.

Head of Opium Den on Rue Amiral Bayle, Cai Bicheng, Appeals; Initial Sentence of Five Years Deemed Fair by Police; Appeal Hearing Concludes, Sentence Set for 22nd 136

In the newly built four-story mansion at numbers 175 and 177 on Rue Amiral Bayle, a loud boom suddenly resounded on the morning of last year's Double Tenth Festival. Flames soared, and disaster struck. Upon hearing the alert, the fire brigade and the Xin Zha police station dispatched firefighters and Chinese and foreign detectives who arrived to extinguish the blaze. Three workers, Gong Baochang, Gong Wenfu, and Miao Zhangcai, were intercepted as they fled the building. Upon entering, it was discovered that the fire was caused by a

Steam Boiler Explosion. The steam boiler was part of equipment used to refine heroin and morphine, and was established by Cai Bicheng, alias Cai Boping, Cai Shizheng, from Hefei, Anhui. Cai resided at number 24 Qinyuan Village, Xin Zha Road. Detectives Cui Chengke and Huang Fusen went to the address to investigate, but Cai had already fled. Subsequently, the First Special District Court interrogated and punished Gong and the other two, and issued an arrest warrant for Cai. It was not until last month that Cui and Huang apprehended Cai at number 179, Route Kroc, in the French Concession and brought him before the First Special Court, which sentenced him to

Five Years Imprisonment, along with a fine of five thousand yuan. However, Cai denied establishing the drug manufacturing operation, and dissatisfied with the conviction and sentence, he hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Yu Xiangqin to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu, along with Judges Su and Zhou, opened the court for the appeal hearing. Prosecutor Zhong Qing also attended to perform his duties. Judge Yu questioned Cai Bicheng, who stated that number 24 Qinyuan Village, Xin Zha Road, was

His Younger Brother's Residence. He himself had lived on Rue Amiral Courbet. In June of last year, his brother returned to his hometown, and died there of illness in July. He then moved to his brother's residence. Around September, a friend surnamed Wang came and said he intended to organize a company with the China Carpet Company, with each share costing 1,500 yuan, totaling 20 shares. He asked Cai to invest in shares. After much persuasion, he reluctantly agreed to purchase one share, but never entered the company, so he was unaware of its contents. On the day of the fire, he went to visit his ailing father at the Qichang Inn. In the evening, he read that day's evening newspaper at the inn, which reported that the Xinghua Company was a

Drug Manufacturing Operation, and had caught fire that morning. The mastermind, Cai, had escaped. He was extremely shocked and immediately called his family, who informed him that the police were searching for him. He dared not return home and temporarily went back to his hometown with his father. He was actually harmed by the Wang fellow. His return to Shanghai was to find Wang and investigate the actual situation in order to turn himself in, but he was arrested instead. The location of the operation was next to the main road and not in a secluded area. How could he have such audacity? If it had been established by him, he would certainly not have

Been Neighbors with His Residence. Furthermore, the three people who testified in the initial trial were unable to provide clear evidence. Therefore, he had filed this appeal, requesting a thorough investigation. He had a 75-year-old mother above him and children under the age of ten below him, who relied on him for support, etc. Lawyers Jiang and Yu then defended him, arguing on the basis of facts and law. Regarding the legal argument,

The Criminal Law Stipulates that manufacturing heroin is punishable by up to five years imprisonment. However, in recent years, those who commit such crimes have rarely been sentenced to the full five years. Yet, Cai was given this heavy sentence, which seems to be an unfair application of the law for the same crime. The initial sentencing was inappropriate and should be reconsidered. Police lawyer Gan Jingxian countered that the initial judgment was very fair, and the defendant had confessed without hesitation. He asked that the appeal be rejected. The court then declared the debate closed, and scheduled the sentencing for the afternoon of the 22nd of this month.

An Extra Corpse Suddenly Found in Old Coffin; Victim Assassinated and Body Moved 139

The area west of the Shanghai South Railway Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, known as Wai Yangqi, is land leased out by the railway. There has been a coffin stored there for many years, yet to be reburied. Yesterday, it was suddenly discovered that the coffin lid had been opened and a new corpse placed inside. The corpse was of a man around thirty years old, wearing a white undershirt and black pants, appearing to be a worker. He had clearly been assassinated before his body was moved there. He had two gunshot wounds in his lower body. The stench was overwhelming. The railway police noticed it and reported it to the police section, who ordered the local bailiff to report it to the local court for inspection. Upon receiving the report, the court dispatched Inspector Kong, along with police officers, to the scene at 4:00 PM yesterday for inspection. It was confirmed that the man had been shot to death and his body moved there. He had two fatal gunshot wounds in his lower abdomen. The other original corpse had decomposed, with only bones remaining. After the inspector completed the examination, he completed the corpse report and ordered the search for the murderer to be investigated and brought to justice. He also ordered the local bailiff to prepare another coffin for burial.

Yongfeng Umbrella Factory Electrocutes Apprentice; Straw Shed Roof Blown Several Dozens of Feet High; Xu Fuqing's Skull Shattered, Instant Death 141

At number 105 in the Siwen Lane of the Datong Road, Xin Zha Road in the Public Concession, the Wang Deji Umbrella Factory had previously been leased and opened by Wang Deji. It is now leased by Zhuang Agui, a local, and renamed the Yongfeng Iron-Handled Umbrella Manufacturing Factory. However, the iron-handled umbrellas require electric welding, so a large straw shed was rented in the western section of the lane to serve as the electric welding workshop. The electric welding work in the factory has been contracted out to He Donghai, who was introduced by the former factory owner, Wang Deji. He is responsible for the electric welding work in the workshop. Yesterday (the 13th) at around 10:00 AM, He went elsewhere for some reason and ordered the apprentice, Xu Fuqing (age 19, from Jingjiang), to do the work. As Xu was holding the welding torch to weld copper, somehow the torch suddenly exploded. With a loud bang, the torch shot upwards, breaking through the straw shed roof and flying dozens of feet high. Xu, seeing the disaster, quickly fled out of the workshop to save his life. Unfortunately, the torch fell from the sky and hit Xu on the top of his head. His skull was shattered instantly, and his brains spilled out. He immediately fell to the ground and died. When the patrolling police heard the sound and rushed to the scene, Xu was already dead in a pool of blood, with a pile of brain matter and a piece of skull next to him. The scene was tragic. They immediately reported to the police chief and ordered detectives to the scene. In addition to sending the body to the forensic examination office on Fielun Road in Hongkou for examination, they also investigated He Donghai, who contracted the electric welding work for the factory, but he had already disappeared. Later, the factory owner, Zhuang Agui, was summoned to the police station to inquire about the circumstances of the accident in order to handle the matter accordingly.

Fangbang Road; Woman Murdered in Broad Daylight; Sheng Caiying Loses Life for Gold Jewelry; Held on to Thief, Pity No Police Came to Help 142

Sheng Caiying, a woman from Sizhou, 21 years old, lived at number 3 in the Shoufu Lane of Taiping Bridge in the French Concession. Yesterday morning at around 10:00 AM, Caiying, holding her two-year-old adopted daughter, Ai Lin, and accompanied by her friend Xu Xiuzhen (25 years old, from Zhenjiang, residing at number 7 in the Lanxin Lane of Route de Geler), and Xu's child Chunlin, went to Xiaodongmen to buy foreign cloth. At around 11:00 AM, they walked to the Fangbang Road area in the city. Sheng Caiying planned to eat snacks in the City God Temple. However, Xu Xiuzhen was eager to return home, so she declined. After walking a few steps, they suddenly encountered a robber, one wearing a blue short-sleeved shirt and pants, and the other wearing a blue long gown, who blocked their way. They forcibly robbed Sheng Caiying of a gold bracelet and a gold watch worn on her wrist, and attempted to escape with the loot. Unexpectedly, Caiying grabbed one of the robbers, shouting for help loudly, angering the robbers. One of the robbers wearing the long gown pulled out a pistol and fired a shot, hitting Caiying in the head, penetrating through the back of her head. Instantly, her brains splattered and she fell to the ground in extreme pain. The two robbers fled north. The Laobeimen Police Station in charge of the area was notified and ordered Inspector Zhang Lantian and other police officers to rush to the scene to surround and arrest the robbers. However, the robbers had already gone far away and could not be apprehended. The wounded Sheng Caiying was sent to the Nanyang Hospital for treatment. However, because the injury was fatal, she died shortly after arriving at the hospital.

Letter to the Editor 150

To the Editor,

I have just read your newspaper's report about the collapse of the foreign-style building in front of number 749 Avenue Joffre and the Fatai Photo Studio, etc., at 3:00 PM on May 10, injuring pedestrians. The police immediately took the landlord, Gao Zhu, the owner of the Fatai Photo Studio, Zhou Ada, and Zhang Puyu, the accountant of Yongtai, as well as the apprentice Lu Fusheng, to the police station. The area in front of the building was not a veranda, but a railing (which was built by the landlord himself). It was also reported that Zhang Zhaoquan was the second landlord and subleased it to Zhou Ada, and that the owner of the Yongtai store was evasive and hiding the truth. After reading this carefully, I was shocked. The owner of the Fatai Photo Studio, Zhou Ada, has been renting from the landlord, Gao Zhu, for more than ten years, while Yongtai has only been there for three years. I am not involved in the lease. Zhang Zhaoquan was not questioned by the police, so there is no question of being evasive and hiding the truth. In summary, the various points mentioned do not correspond to the facts. Please correct the record immediately to avoid spreading misinformation, as it is a matter of great importance to my reputation and responsibility. Please investigate and correct this.

Sincerely,

Zhang Zhaoquan of Yongtai

May 13

Your newspaper mistakenly printed Zhang Shaoquan as Zhang Zhaoquan.

Three Crew Members of the Jiahe Steamer Released After Ransom Paid; After Six Months in Bandits' Den, They Are En Route to Shanghai 153

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiahe steamer was hijacked last year, and three crew members were kidnapped, demanding a huge ransom. It has been half a year since then. The families of the hostages have repeatedly negotiated the ransom, going through four rounds. It was not until this time that the families personally went to Hong Kong to negotiate with the bandits, and then the three were released. They are now on their way and are expected to arrive in Shanghai on Thursday. The details are as follows:

The Jiahe Hijacking Incident: The Jiahe steamer was hijacked by pirates on November 4 last year in Shantou. The twelve pirates intended to steal 300,000 yuan in new banknotes, but the new banknotes had not been stamped and could not be used. They were robbed of more than 2,000 yuan in cash and shot and killed航警 Yang Zetian. Before leaving, they kidnapped the business director, Shen Qinxiang, the tallyman, Ge Liangchen, and the accountant, Li Xiaobin. The three were taken to the Dapeng Bay island and hidden, in order to demand a huge ransom.

Four Rounds of Ransom Negotiations: For the issue of redeeming the three hostages, negotiations have been held four times with the pirates' representatives in Hong Kong. The first three times, the ransom demanded by the bandits was too high, sometimes 20,000 yuan, sometimes 60,000 yuan. The representatives sent by the families of the hostages had no results from the negotiations and had already spent more than 1,000 yuan. They had to withdraw to Shanghai, expressing their willingness to abandon the negotiations and leave the hostages to the bandits' disposal. Until the fourth time last month, the bandits voluntarily reduced the ransom and asked the three families to go to negotiate in person.

Families Go to Negotiate in Person: On March 22, the families of the three hostages took the Anxing steamer from Shanghai to Hong Kong for the final negotiations with the pirates' representatives. The ransom for the three hostages was at most 2,000 yuan each. After the families arrived in Hong Kong, they spent a long time negotiating for a month before finally reaching an agreement with the bandits and redeeming Shen, Li, and Ge. Each family paid the bandits a certain amount (the amount is unknown and will be known when they arrive in Shanghai). The bandit leader then released the three hostages and handed them over to their families to bring them back to Shanghai.

Departed Hong Kong for Shanghai: Shen Qinxiang, Li Xiaobin, and Ge Liangchen, the three hostages, were released from the bandits' den after the families paid the ransom last month. The bandits led them to Hong Kong and handed them over to their families to bring them back to Shanghai. Shen, Li, and Ge have now telegraphed from Hong Kong to Shanghai, saying that they have escaped from the bandits' den and are taking the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiheng steamer from Hong Kong, accompanied by their families, back to Shanghai. They are expected to arrive on Thursday (the 16th).

Shangguan Min defrauded funds and absconded, eloping with a dancing girl to Hong Kong and Guangdong, resorting to this tactic due to failed speculation, and was arrested upon returning to Shanghai in front of the police station 154

Shangguan Min Geng, also known as Chen Shaoying, a native of Hai Ning, is currently twenty-five years old. He previously worked as an accountant at Shen Da Transportation Company at 504 Edward Road. Because he was fond of pleasure-seeking, indulged in song and dance halls, and also engaged in speculation that failed, his income could not cover his expenses, resulting in a huge deficit that he could not make up for. Therefore, on October 15th of last year, he used a worthless check from the Central Trust Company to exchange checks with Jiang Lian'en, the acting accountant of the company, and defrauded them of 7,300 yuan in foreign currency.

He abandoned his job and absconded without a trace. Gao Zijia, the general manager of Shen Da Company, reported the situation to the police station, requesting the First Special Court to issue an arrest warrant. Meanwhile, Shen Da Company published a reward notice offering 1,000 yuan in foreign currency for his arrest. It was not until around 8 PM on the 11th of this month that Shangguan Min Geng was arrested and detained in front of the Chengdu Road Police Station by Chinese detective Shi Shanqing and Western detective Gai Zilai. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, and Qian Xunjiu, the legal representative of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Legal Department,

filed a lawsuit in accordance with Articles 363 and 366 of the Criminal Law for fraud and breach of trust, detailing the course of events. He stated that on October 24th of last year, Gao Zijia, the general manager of Shen Da Company, reported to the police station that Shangguan Min Geng, the company's accountant in charge of books, had used fraudulent means to defraud them of 7,300 yuan in foreign currency, which he squandered outside, and became intimate with Gao Xiaomeimei, a dancing girl from the Yangtze Dance Hall.

They eloped with the money. As for his fraudulent method, he exchanged a Ningtou check from the Central Trust Company with Jiang Lian'en, the accountant in charge of money, for a check from the company to be cashed. It was discovered that the company's money accounting room was originally expanded and appointed by Shangguan Tingmu, a cousin of the defendant. At that time, Shangguan Tingmu happened to be in Hangzhou, so Jiang Yun'en was acting as his agent. The defendant took advantage of this opportunity to deceive and exchange the checks, and so on. Upon receiving the report, the police station

had no other clues to find. They had to start with the dancing girl Gao Xiaomeimei and learned that Miss Gao lived on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. Chinese and Western detectives went to investigate. According to Miss Gao's mother, her daughter had not returned for several days and her whereabouts were unknown. It was not until October 28th that Gao Xiaomeimei suddenly surrendered to the police station and explained the situation. She said that she met the defendant, who, on October 18th, used the alias Chen Shaoying and asked Miss Gao to travel to Hong Kong with him. They then took the Suzhou ship and left Shanghai for Hong Kong. They stayed at the New China Hotel

for four nights and then went to Quanzhou, staying at the Zhongshan Hotel for four days as well. Later, because Miss Gao had to return to Shanghai for business, Chen returned to Shanghai with her and stayed at Miss Gao's house for several days. Because Chen insisted on going to Suzhou, Miss Gao sent him to the station and bid him farewell. Therefore, according to her speculation, Chen must be in Suzhou, and so on. The police station immediately requested the court to issue an arrest warrant. However, after investigation, it was found that the defendant had sent a letter to Gao Zijia from Hong Kong, stating that he had failed in speculation with his friend Zhang Keming in trading national bonds and had

no way to make up for it. He had to borrow a large sum of money from the company. Later, he intended to commit suicide, but was stopped by his friend Zhang, who provided him with 700 yuan in foreign currency, so he planned to go to England to seek employment, and so on. In fact, what he said in the letter was all fictitious. He was actually eloping with the dancing girl he loved to Hong Kong. Because the police station only stated in his letter that he was in Hong Kong, without a specific location, there was no way to investigate. It was not until the day before yesterday that the defendant was arrested in front of the police station. According to the defendant's confession in the police station, he

originally intended to turn himself in, but he did not have the courage, so he lingered in front of the police station and wrote a confession, detailing the course of events of using the money. Judging from his sad words, there was a sense of regret. The confession was submitted to the case and a request was made to postpone the hearing. When questioned, the defendant Shangguan Min Geng confessed that he had failed in speculation and initially only owed his friend Zhang Keming more than 1,000 yuan in foreign currency. Later, he was encouraged by Zhang, who said that the

market was good at the time and that a lot could be made. Therefore, I exchanged a check from the Central Trust Company due on the 9th of a certain month with Jiang for a check from Shen Da due on the 5th. After cashing it, I first paid off the previous debt of more than 1,000 yuan and then gave Zhang another 3,500 yuan, instructing him to buy and sell when he saw an opportunity. Unexpectedly, after Zhang got the money, he avoided meeting me. Although I went to the Yangtze Dance Hall many times to look for him, I could not find him. Later, according to a friend, Zhang had already gone to Hong Kong, so I eloped with Gao Xiaomeimei to follow him. In

Hong Kong and Guangdong, I searched all the dance halls but could not find him. I also saw the advertisement from my cousin, so I returned to Shanghai. However, at that time, I still had 2,000 yuan in cash with me and wanted to find a way to deal with it. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Shanghai, I saw the wanted advertisement again. I felt that this small amount of 2,000 yuan was of no help, so I did not dare to go there. The day before yesterday, I was actually at the gate of the police station and was not arrested, and so on. Judge Yang verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be detained and await a postponed hearing on Friday.

In addition to exhibiting hygiene models and charts at each district venue, Wang Shufang was invited to broadcast a speech on the significance of hygiene movements.

Jiangsu Province Revises the Tooth Tax Regulations for Various Counties 160

The tooth tax item in Jiangsu's education funding accounts for about one-sixth of the province's total education expenditure. The tax collection methods are divided into commercial bidding and recognized handling. This year, the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office revised these tooth tax regulations, and they are now being implemented in accordance with the new regulations. The following are excerpts from the two regulations:

Jiangsu Province's Regulations on Commercial Bidding for Tooth Tax in Various Counties (1) The tooth tax of each county shall be handled through commercial bidding in accordance with the resolution of the Education Funding Committee and the collection method of slaughter tax. (2) The bidding date for each county shall be set by this office. Bids shall be submitted in a sealed box, and personnel shall be sent by the Education Funding Committee to monitor the process. (3) This office shall determine a base amount for the tooth tax of each county. When merchants submit bids, they shall prepare a cash deposit equivalent to one-twentieth of the base amount as a guarantee and submit it to this office (Education Funding Management Office) in advance for inspection and exchange for a bidding ticket. The determined total amount shall be filled in according to the format and put into the box. This office shall open the bids publicly to determine the highest bidder. If two or more bidders offer the same amount, the old merchant shall be given priority. If there is no old merchant, the bids with the same amount may be re-submitted publicly. (4) The deposit paid by the winning bidder shall be deducted from the deposit to be paid. The deposits of unsuccessful bidders shall be returned on the spot. (5) Once a merchant wins the bid, they shall obtain joint guarantees from two or more reputable stores, and after verifying the recognized amount, they shall pay two-tenths of the cash deposit in advance within three days and submit it to this office for verification. No public bonds, stocks, or other items shall be used to offset the payment to avoid trickery. If the deposit cannot be paid in full within the time limit, or if the bid is won but not processed, the bidding right shall be revoked immediately, and the deposit paid shall be confiscated in full. The next highest bidder shall take over the bid. (6) The recognition period is limited to one year. If there is no tax arrears within the time limit, the deposit shall be deducted in the last month of the term. (7) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be revised at any time.

Jiangsu Province's Regulations on Recognized Handling of Tooth Tax in Various Counties (1) All grades, industries, and tax rates for handling this tooth tax shall be handled in accordance with the tooth industry regulations of this office. If there are any reductions in grades or combined collections due to local customs or commercial depression, the old practices shall be maintained to show consideration. If a recognized merchant is accused of harsh collection or fraud, they shall be punished immediately after investigation and verification. (2) The recognized amount of tooth tax is limited to a short term. The county government shall continue to handle the long-term registration of business taxes and cocoon ticket taxes. (3) If there are educational construction and other surcharges for the tooth tax of each county, the recognized merchant shall collect them in accordance with the existing regulations and report and remit them to the relevant authorities separately, which are not included in the recognized amount of this office. (4) The merchant shall determine the recognized amount and prepare a table of peak and off-peak months, which shall be submitted to this office for verification and approval for monthly remittance. (5) After the merchant determines the recognized amount, they shall report and remit it according to the amount. They shall not ask for reductions or resign midway to prevent trickery. (6) The merchant shall apply to this office in advance for the registration certificates and notices required for the collection of tooth tax, which shall be transferred to the Finance Department for printing and distribution for filling and use. No private receipts shall be issued to prevent fraud. (7) If a tooth household resists tax, it shall be reported to the county government or the Public Security Bureau for investigation and handling. No private penalties shall be imposed to avoid harassment. (8) The merchant who handles this tooth tax shall collect taxes from each tooth in accordance with the regulations. They shall not subcontract to avoid abuses. (9) The recognized amount is of a contracted nature. Regardless of whether the tax revenue is surplus or deficit, the merchant shall be responsible for remitting the full amount. No shortage is allowed. (10) Every month, at the end of the month, the merchant shall prepare a report in accordance with the six forms issued by this office, together with the payment receipts and old certificates, and submit them for verification. No delays are allowed. If the report is not submitted, it will be impossible to verify how many certificates have been used and how many remain. The issuance of certificates will not be approved to ensure caution. (11) All monthly reports must be filled in truthfully. There must be no concealment or falsification of tooth households. If the personnel sent by this office find that the tooth households do not match the forms, they shall be investigated and punished. (12) Of the one-tenth handling fee under the registration tax item, two cents shall be remitted directly to the county government, two cents shall be remitted to the Finance Department, one cent shall be reported and remitted to this office, and the remaining five cents shall be retained by the merchant for office expenses. (13) The aforementioned handling fee shall be reported and remitted separately according to the actual amount collected, not based on the recognized amount. (14) The aforementioned handling fee is collected separately under the registration tax item and is different from the slaughter tax public fee. It shall not be calculated within the recognized amount. (15) The Finance Department's two cents handling fee is currently collected on behalf of this office. It must be paid to the treasury every month, and the treasury receipt shall be sent directly to this office. Do not issue the wrong treasury receipt to avoid trouble. If the county is remote and far from the treasury, cash may be remitted by the post office for transfer to the Finance Department. (16) The educational treasury designates the China Communications Bank and the Jiangsu Bank for reporting and remitting tax payments. Be sure to hand them over to the three banks directly. Do not make mistakes. (17) The payments for month A must be cleared in the middle of month B. If delayed, the committee will propose it. If it is not resolved after two months, the recognition case will be revoked, and the deposit will be used to offset the payment. If it is not enough, the county will be ordered to recover the payment. (18) If the merchant fulfills the one-year term and reports and remits the amount in full every month, and the monthly report is excellent, the renewal of the term may be approved depending on the circumstances to encourage them. (19) When the merchant hands over at the end of the term, all tooth industries that have not expired shall not reduce the tax collection, and the certificates shall be filled in first. If there is any fraud, the successor shall investigate and report it, and the merchant shall be punished by ten times the amount obtained. (20) When the merchant hands over at the end of the term, all registration certificates and notices used and remaining shall be transferred to the successor in full for continued filling and use. If there is any shortage, a fine of 50 yuan per sheet shall be imposed in accordance with the previous tax regulations of the Finance Department. (21) After the merchant hands over the business at the end of the term, all tooth household files, documents, and registration certificates shall be transferred to the successor for counting, and the new and old merchants shall jointly report to this office for record within five days. No delays are allowed. (22) The merchant who handles the tooth tax shall be given the title of director and a bell shall be issued to show good faith, in accordance with the slaughter tax recognized merchant method. (23) The tooth industry regulations of this office shall apply, except for the long-term tooth tax handled by the county and Article 8, which shall be handled separately. (24) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, this office may revise them at any time.

The Education Bureau Bans Zhenhong Elementary School 164

The private Zhenhong Elementary School on Tangshan Road, Jishan Lane, Hongkou, this port, is a disguised reorganization of the former Yuqing Elementary School. Yuqing Elementary School did not apply for registration. Principal Tan Yanwu recently sold the school and school equipment to Hu Xu and others due to the school's finances being unsustainable and renamed it Zhenhong Elementary School. It neither reported the reorganization nor applied for registration. After investigation by the personnel sent by the Municipal Education Bureau, the Public Concession Council was requested to strictly ban it. It is heard that there are many other schools of the same nature in this city. The Municipal Education Bureau will also investigate them all and take strict measures to avoid misleading children.

Since the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee appointed Chen Zhongfu as the director of the Zhenru District Office, it immediately began preliminary survey work, once discussed with the persons in charge of the municipal office, police station, security corps, and municipal primary schools in the district, convened two preparatory meetings, decided on the general outline of the literacy survey work, and convened more than 30 people including local security guards, police officers, and school representatives in the district at Jinan University on the 9th of this month to hold a symposium and dinner, chaired by Chen Zhongfu, director of the office, and performed the etiquette as usual. The specific methods for conducting the survey, such as the division of district maps, the distribution of police officers and local security guards, the accommodation and meal expenses of the survey personnel, and the regulations on work procedures and dates, were all submitted for resolution and implementation of specific measures. Foreign Educators Pay Attention to the February 2nd Movement and are Particularly Interested in Popular Education Vehicles 169

The purpose of the February 2nd Movement is to "promote local goods, implement social savings, strive for social production, develop the national economy, improve the people's livelihood, and collaborate for the revival of the Chinese nation." It is an education that tests the people's livelihood as the foundation. Through the efforts of Tai Shuangqiu, Tang Maohuai, and others, it has had an amazing development in the past two years and has long been known to all sectors of society in China. This movement has now attracted the attention of foreign educators. Professor Melvin of the Teachers College of New York University recently sent a letter to the February 2nd Movement Promotion Association at 2631 Zhongshan Road, Shanghai, stating that "the February 2nd Movement is the most meaningful educational movement in China today. I deeply believe that it will have rapid development to achieve the goal of reviving the national economy and will be assisted by the government as a giant in China's popular education. I wrote an article in the China Review Weekly five years ago discussing that China needs an education that is suitable for the economic environment and the interests of the people. At that time, no one paid attention to it. Now this February 2nd Movement is of great significance to the country and the international community. Please send a copy of the photos of the movement, especially the photos of the popular education vehicle and its implementation activities, so that I can write articles and promote it in American newspapers."

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 185

— (Yan BOGuang)

Last year's autumn harvest was affected by drought, and most of the farmland yielded nothing. This spring, hungry people are everywhere, crying for food. Moreover, families with more children suffer even more from hunger, and they have no choice but to sell their children to avoid starvation. According to investigations, girls are easier to sell than boys, and those with beautiful faces are especially popular with buyers. These girls are all bought by big cities, taught to sing and dance, and in a few years, they may reveal their talents and become stars. This shows that women are indeed more valuable than men.

The weather is gradually getting warmer, and people's clothes are gradually becoming lighter, especially for women, who have already changed into the latest fashions. On the prosperous Nanjing Road in Shanghai, you can see many sensual women—bare legs, bare arms—and most sexually aroused men can't help but exclaim—wonderful—right? But in the countryside, there are also very healthy young women, barefoot, bare thighs, rolling up their sleeves, helping men transplant rice in the fields. Who pays attention to them?

Whispers of Willow Catkins 186

— Qiu Zi

Willow catkins are terribly annoying! The willow flowers fly, ruining everything, a good picture of miscellaneous flowers and trees, and noisy Orioles flying about the beautiful scenery of Jiangnan, all being spoiled by it.

Originally, willow catkins are inherently frivolous, inherently weak, drifting with the wind, completely involuntary. Sometimes, when falling on people's books, it turns into bookworms, eating away at the books. If it falls into a green grass pond, it becomes duckweed, drifting with the waves. During this season of willow catkins, wool and leather must not be exposed to the sun. Therefore, the ancients described frivolous women as "water-like willow catkins," which is simply the most appropriate metaphor.

As for "willow catkin radish," it refers to the small, red, and round radish that is only available when there are willow catkins, and naturally disappears afterward. Willow catkin radish, radish willow catkins, they come together and go together. Sister flowers? Difficult brothers?

The ancients had leisurely moods, "idly watching children catching willow catkins," living the life of a leisure class. Others saw "dots of willow catkins falling into the inkstone," and felt that the spring scenery would not last long, burying themselves in reading the Zhou Yi. Now, crazy willow catkins are dancing in the wind again. This clearly shows to us that "ninety days of spring are about to pass." Friends! Are you excited from this moment on? Does it matter at all?

Hired Carriages 187

— Yan

In Shanghai, taking a hired carriage is not considered grand, because there are friends who own automobiles to overshadow it. However, in inland cities, where streets are narrow and automobiles are useless, those who ride in hired carriages are unique and supreme, exuding an awe-inspiring presence. Although the hired carriages are the same as those in Shanghai, the sounds they emit to clear the way are even more impressive than Shanghai automobiles. Their loudspeaker has two parts: one makes a "coo-coo" sound, and the other makes a "ding-ding-dang-dang" sound. The "coo-coo" sound is as majestic as a lion's roar, and the "ding-ding-dang-dang" sound is as clear and melodious as the clash of gold and stone. Sometimes "coo-coo," sometimes "ding-dang," sometimes "coo-coo ding-dang," they alternate in concert, creating a truly imposing and dignified atmosphere that can make everyone give way. One can leisurely recline in the carriage, right leg crossed over the left, looking around with an air of superiority. How arrogant and enviable!

Hired carriages in Changshu are even more extravagant than those elsewhere. In addition to the advantages of hired carriages in other places, they have a special nighttime splendor. Their carriages are equipped with bright searchlights, with at least two lights on the sides and up to four lights including the rear. Compared to the hired carriages of Shanghai courtesans who have connections, their exquisiteness and brightness are unmatched. A carriage in the street, with a young master sitting inside, the snow-like light and jade-like face reflecting each other, may not win a carriage full of fruit thrown as admiration, but it attracts the attention of thousands, especially winning the favor of beauties, which is enough to be proud of. Since the carriage is so exquisite and dazzling, the coachman must also be neat and tidy to match the carriage. Therefore, the coachmen are often well-dressed, in light summer clothes and warm winter furs. In the cold season, when the coachmen run, they must lift the two lower corners of their long fur coats and tuck them under their belts, ostensibly to make running easier, but in reality, it is to deliberately expose their snow-white fur, showing off their wealth. The coachman's attire is enough to show off his wealth, and the person in the carriage feels even wealthier for having such a coachman.

Do readers doubt my words? Then you should know that Wuxi, Changshu, and other places have many beautiful mountains and rivers. Taking advantage of the bright spring scenery, you might as well go there for sightseeing and, by the way, appreciate their hired carriages.

A Quick Sketch of the Buddha Bathing Festival 189

— Dun

Buddha Bathing Festival: people, men and women, old and young, devout believers with yellow cloth bags, vendors shouting east and west, incense smoke, candlelight, paper ingot scraps... These intertwine to form the annual grand gathering. Although this kind of hustle and bustle happens every year, people still flock in large groups to the Jing'an Temple.

Believers take out shiny silver coins from their bags, exchange them for incense sticks, red candles, and paper ingots at the temple gate, and walk into the temple. In the blink of an eye, the paper ingots turn to ashes, and the incense sticks and red candles are moved away by the temple monks. A faint smile floats on the believers' faces, and they are squeezed into the crowd again. As they step out of the side door of the temple, a Christian gives them a leaflet that says "Do not worship idols." They glance sideways, quickly throw the reactionary slogan to the ground, and seem to say in their mouths: "Bad luck—touching India!"

There is a square well in front of the temple. Some believers buy turtles in the temple and release them into the well, but the well water is very shallow. Vendors often wait for the believers to walk away and then catch the turtles and sell them to the second person. This cyclical and humorous release technique can only be found in the city.

The area around the temple is crowded with stalls, tables, chairs, and rattanware. The open space on the left is a group of various gadgets: peep shows, candy stalls, turntables... All kinds of money-making businesses. With the market downturn, there are more viewers than buyers, and the vendors frown even more under the heavy rain.

The Fleeting Fragrance of the Imperial Incense 191

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

After this loud shout, there was a great commotion. The dogs on one side of the doghouse quickly ran out. "Woof... woof... woof..." they barked in a chaotic manner, wagging their short tails like crazy, clearly indicating that they were welcoming the Empress Dowager. Seeing this, the Empress Dowager couldn't help but beam with joy, even more pleased than when she received the obeisance of her ministers. Among this group of dogs, the one the Empress Dowager loved the most, named Hailong—which was the one that later followed us to Fengtian—was also among them; this time, I recognized its special talent for the first time. When it saw us, it stood up straight, shrinking its front legs, making a gesture like a bow. Its meaning seemed to be:

"Look! Who else here can be so clever? If I didn't have such a special skill that made other dogs look inferior, how would the Empress Dowager especially favor me?"

However, it couldn't maintain that upright posture for very long, only for about four or five minutes, before it fell back down; I think it was probably because standing up straight was really exhausting, so the animal couldn't last.

We gradually got closer to the doghouses, and the eunuch on duty that day began to gather the dogs that had already come out of the house. Seeing that some were lagging behind and had not yet noticed, he shouted even louder; in this way, they all ran out together. (313)

Real Jokes 192

— (Drunk Madman)

I have two friends, A and B: one is impatient, and the other is slow. Now I will list their amusing stories below to bring a smile.

A likes to drink very much: One day, he passed by a liquor store, and he was a regular customer. He asked the waiter to heat up a pot of wine and took it home himself. When he got home, his wife saw that her husband had brought back a pot of wine. She prepared cups and chopsticks to pour wine for him. But when she picked up the wine pot, it was empty. Surprised, she asked, "Huh! Why is this pot empty and has no wine?" A said, "Because the aroma of the wine rushed to my nose, I had a sudden craving for wine, and I couldn't wait to get home. So, I drank it while walking, and when I got home, the wine was finished."

B is very slow: He subscribes to several major and minor newspapers and wants to read them at night. He reads each one carefully, not willing to miss anything. In this way, he has to read each newspaper carefully according to the day it was published. One night, he picked up a supplement of the China Report to read. A friend happened to come and asked, "What's new in today's newspaper?" B slowly said, "There may be something new. But I read the newspaper according to the schedule. The newspaper I am reading now is still from before this week. Today's newspaper has not been reached yet."

Personal Anecdotes

Record of Gao Zhifang (Part 1) 193

— Pillow Green

"Former master Mr. Zhang's esteemed inspection, your humble servant Gao Zhifang pays his respects. Currently serving at the Xinzha branch of the police force."

One morning last month, a young servant suddenly came into the room and woke me up, handing me this note written in ink, saying that a person who looked like a policeman wanted to see me and had written this note; he said that he hadn't seen his old employer for many years and had come to greet me today and report on his experiences; he could even call out the names of several of my children. I saw that the handwriting was not very good and was also very unfamiliar. After inquiring about this person's appearance, build, and accent, I guessed among the hundreds of people who had eaten at my house in the past, but I couldn't figure out who it was. My eldest daughter went out to peek and rushed back in excitedly to tell me: "It's rickshaw puller A-Gen! Really, he's wearing a police uniform, very new, shaking!" So I told the young servant to ask him to come back in the morning another day, so we could talk more.

This Gao Zhifang is from Jiangbei. He served at my place six or seven years ago; at that time, some people knew that his home was located in the Xuejia Hong area of the South City, in a dilapidated boat with a high deck along the Huangpu River bank. That place was originally a settlement for Jiangbei compatriots, all using the same type of dry boat as their home. He worked as a rickshaw puller, first pulling a rickshaw for a distant relative of mine—a very successful businessman. However, he thought this employer was too vulgar and didn't get along with him, not caring about earning a few extra dollars from him. He could read and write, and whenever he had free time, he would pick up books and newspapers to read, sometimes even reading aloud, which people called him a bookworm. This was also disliked by his employer, who resented that he seemed to be deliberately trying to compete with the employer in qualifications. He also wholeheartedly entrusted a senior relative of mine to bring him to my house; his idea was that because Mr. Zhang was a scholar, he wanted to serve a refined master. Soon, he got his wish and came to my place to work, and he could freely read the available police reports when he had time. In this way, after about a year, he returned to his hometown for some reason and couldn't come out for a while, so he stopped doing business at my place. After that, we didn't hear any news from him until recently.

Sure enough, after a few days, this former rickshaw puller A-Gen, now a police officer Gao Zhifang, came as scheduled. He immediately stood at attention and saluted when he saw me, which made me feel somewhat uneasy; as for him, he still maintained the title of former servant, only standing while talking. I heard the outline of his past.

At that time, when he returned to Shanghai from his hometown, he changed to pulling a yellow rickshaw to make a living, and the situation was even worse than pulling a rickshaw; fortunately, he was an insider, ran fast, and was young—over eleven or twelve years old—so he was still able to barely make a living.

Finance: Gold Market Calm Before Swap, Result Rebounds by 1.2 Yuan 194

The gold market started yesterday with ups and downs, and the market was quite stable. With the depletion of chips, buying interest was easily stimulated. The Guangdong banks continued to support foreign exchange, so that although the Indian silver reported an increase, there was still an upward trend. The one-day settlement slightly rebounded. In the early morning, due to the consistent rise in overseas silver markets, the forward silver price in Montreal even rose by more than one point, and the exchange rate rose slightly. The price of raw gold in London fell by one penny, and people's hearts continued to weaken. Over-the-counter pre-market trading opened, retreating to 84.5 yuan, and supply exceeded demand, falling back to around 3 yuan. The central bank's listing was announced, with the British price unchanged and the American price rising. The customs gold unit fell by 1 li, and the gold standard retreated to 834.6 yuan. The morning opened with a low market, but although the Jewish broker Cho Zhifubu was plugging, the banks were still supporting, and it rose. Large households took advantage of the high price to sell, anticipating that HSBC's listing would show the British price unchanged and the American price rising by 0.0625, with a slight downstream. However, because the Guangdong banks were vigorously supporting the pound, the foreign exchange market tightened and rose again. The banks took advantage of the high price to force the sale, and rumors such as the arrival of spot goods and the expectation of high silver prices fueled the selling sentiment, suddenly turning weak and falling. However, because large households took advantage of the low price to buy in, the table was depleted, and the price repeatedly rebounded after the low. Finally, the foreign exchange market stabilized, and the market turned to a hovering trend. The later market initially reported an increase of 14 annas in Indian silver and then fell, but because the London market was ordinary, buyers took advantage of the low price to move, and rumors of favorable news caused a buying spree due to the extremely depleted supply, skyrocketing rapidly. Although the price fluctuated after the high, the domestic market tightened due to the Guangdong banks' vigorous support for the US dollar, and the price rose. The banks took advantage of the high price to sell, and large households also sold, but the buying interest was still strong. After that, there were repeated ups and downs, and the hovering was uncertain. The second return of Indian silver was small, with one anna having little impact. The in-house price fell slightly due to a large supply order, but the overall trend remained hovering. The entire day's market was very mediocre. With the swap approaching, the market lacked a large demand for supply. After recording the one-day market,

The morning opened at 783.5 yuan, a decrease of 2 yuan compared to the previous Saturday. Fuxing, Yongda, Decheng, Richang, Changda, Hengchang, Yongheng and others have all accepted. The June pound settlement of 1.875 gradually rose to 8.5 yuan. Nabi came out with the US dollar for May, and Hengyu, Fuxing, Yongyi, and Cheng Hui sold at a high price, falling back to 5.6 yuan. Dadecheng and Hui took advantage of the low price to accept them, but they were still stable. It was anticipated that HSBC's listing would show the British price unchanged and the American price rising by 0.0625. At this time, it was extremely stable. Afterwards, Shengda vigorously supported the June pound 1.875 without giving up. Fuxing, Yongda, Decheng, Huixiang, Yongde, and Yisheng jointly purchased the clause, gradually rising to 8.5 yuan. Tongtai, Changtong, and Fengheng sold at a high price and fell. Changda, Fuxing, Yongqian, Changxiang, Huixiang, Fuyu, Dadecheng, Hengyu, and Chunyuan successively sold the clause. News that spot goods had arrived in Tianjin and that silver prices were expected to rise caused the price to fall to 3 yuan. Dadecheng and Xingyong took advantage of the low price to buy in, rising to 4.5 yuan. Hengyu, Huixiang, Shunmao, and Dacheng sold the clause, and it fell to 1.8 yuan. Yisheng, Fuxing, Shui Dadecheng, Fuyu and others took advantage of the low price to accept the clause, rising to 4.4 yuan. Jiakun and Hengxing sold the clause, and it still fell to 3.1 yuan. MacGregor purchased the July US dollar 8.125. Yuanchang, Yongfuxing, Yongrichang, Fuyu, and retail investors entered the clause, and it rose to 5.6 yuan. Grains: Actual Sales Groups Spit Out Futures Flour 202

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, prices for various months showed a pattern of near-term declines and far-term rallies, but ultimately fell back step by step. With quotations for imported wheat, Chicago fell by about 1.24 cents, and Canada fell by 0.08 to 0.10 cents. When pricing began, imported wheat was quoted lower. The Tianjin-Beijing area also experienced heavy rain, and market sentiment there had already loosened. The customer groups, upon receiving this information, uniformly sold off after the market opened, causing prices to fall by two to three cents. However, in September and October, outside buyers actively bought in large quantities, supporting the market sentiment. Afterwards, customer groups sold, while outsiders bought in, and the strength of both forces was substantial. Trading volume reached over 800,000. However, once the actual sales groups sold, market sentiment turned weary. When the market opened in the afternoon, because the actual sales groups returned to selling, market sentiment was uniformly bearish. Buyers were not as active as in the morning, and the market fell back step by step. If the actual sales groups continue to be bearish, prices may fall further. As a result, the current month fell by 4.75 cents, June-July fell by 4.25 cents, August fell by 4.75 cents, September fell by 4.25 cents, and October fell by 3 cents.

Sharp Decline in Futures Wheat 203

Yesterday, after the futures wheat market opened in the morning, prices for various months were flat and lackluster. With quotations for imported wheat, Chicago fell by about 2.14 cents, and Canada fell by 0.08 to 0.10 cents. When pricing began, imported wheat continued to decline. Although there were storms in local and outport areas, the extent of damage to the new wheat was unclear. Furthermore, imported wheat could continue to be ordered, so even if there were minor domestic issues, international trade could still proceed. Therefore, market sentiment was weary when pricing began, down two to three cents from the previous week. When the market opened in the afternoon, because the decline in the flour market was frightening, and news spread that another ship of Australian wheat had been booked at 4.75 yuan, market sentiment uniformly loosened. Although trading was not very active, the decline was substantial, reaching about 10 cents. It is observed that during the new trading period, the fluctuations are huge, and because the stakes are high, market sentiment is easily swayed. As a result, the current month fell by 10 cents, August fell by 11 cents, and September fell by 11 cents. The current wheat market has stabilized, and deliveries are still active.
