On Popular Literature 210

— Xia Shi

Now is the era of "popularization."

However, the general public seems to retain the traditional concept of the term "popularization" and often misunderstands it. Take literature, for example. When popular literature is mentioned, it is assumed to cater to low-level tastes, different from and even opposed to the pure literature of scholars and celebrities. This is the same view as the Book of Han's "Treatise on Literature," which sees novels as "created from street gossip and hearsay."

In fact, the current meaning of "popularization" should not be like this. It is not about catering to low-level tastes, but about raising the level of general readers' tastes. Popular literature and pure literature becoming opposing terms originated when literature was seized by a few. Those few scholars, in order to flaunt their profound knowledge and prove that the general public was unworthy of approaching literature, called works that originated from or catered to the tastes of the general public popular literature, indicating that they could not be classified as orthodox literature. However, the upward development of the general public's life finally inspired the consciousness of demanding literature. They were not satisfied with low-level tastes. They wanted to break through that artificial barrier and enter the "palace of art." Therefore, the popular literature movement that arose from this is clearly different from the previous view. It is not about establishing a separate school, but about fundamentally making literature a universal thing. Otherwise, why don't we call Zhang Henshui and Bu Ken Sheng popular literature writers? Why don't we recognize *Tixiao Yinyuan* and *Jianghu Qixia Zhuan* as works of popular literature?

"Popularization" refers to both content and form. Simply circling around in form cannot be considered popularization, and talking about content without considering form cannot be considered popularization either. *Jianghu Qixia Zhuan* is relatively simple in terms of writing, but because it expresses a low-level taste, we cannot recognize it as a work of popular literature. The difference between low-level taste and high-level taste lies in the fact that low-level taste is a stale taste without life content or incompatible with life content, while high-level taste is a taste felt from real life or that can strengthen life force.

In terms of content, "popularization" should be universal and positive. In terms of form, it should be concise and brisk. The purpose of popular literature is to make literature accessible to the general public. Therefore, the popular literature movement cannot be viewed solely from the perspective of popularization, but must be seen as the linchpin of the entire development of literature.

Country Road 211

— Lu Fen

Having moved more than a thousand li south, the climate is somewhat warmer, though I can't quite discern it yet. But the trees and wheat clearly indicate it.

A few years ago, I traveled this road often. No matter which end I started from, it always gave me a diligent kind of pleasure. Whether riding a donkey or taking a rickshaw, I was always happy, because I loved the countryside yet couldn't leave the city.

My hometown is on the green earth, on the lush plains, where no waterways run.

In such a world, the automobile is the only hero. A sign across the car's front reads: "Bound for Dongzhou," I don't know what it means. After weighing the luggage, a check at the city gate, and we were released. Seems quite impressive. But shortly after crossing the railway, this hero ran into a snag – its head was stuck under a bridge.

"Get out, get out..." A young driver opened the car door.

So everyone got out.

"Ah, what happened?"

A middle-aged woman poked half her head out of the car window. No one paid her any attention.

Somehow, one of the car wheels had fallen into the water, gone for a bath.

So, repairs. Oil can, pliers, wrenches were all brought out. Villagers held rice bowls, village children stuffed their mouths until they bulged, and crowded around, as if watching an animal that had died by the roadside.

The driver, eyes bulging, raised a forefinger and shook it in the air, cursing:

"Damn you good-for-nothings, get lost!"

The villagers looked at each other, and silently dispersed, because the car company was government-run, and a wheel had fallen into the water; it was best not to provoke them.

During travels, we often encounter unpleasant pleasantries, such as insults and beatings. People probably don't love peace as much as they sing, living in constant and unchanging circumstances, they feel an innate unpleasantness, depression, or predicament. When someone starts an argument, others are naturally happy to watch, as long as it doesn't involve them. Not even a single hair is allowed to be plucked. However, it doesn't work that way. In a car or on a boat, being jostled and kicked is inevitable; listening to others argue makes it difficult to have peace and quiet. Travelers often hope that something unusual will happen, but only as long as it doesn't interfere with them.

Luckily, people climbed back into the rectangular box. Thirteen in all, five of whom were "our people," riding without tickets.

"My eyes are going to cry themselves blind, drive faster. You want the horse to run well, but you don't want it to eat... you have it easy!"

The postal worker spoke with a Beijing accent. He had a child-like round head, and a naive smile floated on his full face.

Another rogue-like young companion, for some reason twisted his face to the side, and tapped his knee with two fingers, saying:

"As for you: hugging thighs."

The driver leaned his upper body forward, the hero roared and trembled again, woo, woo, woo! And so everyone swayed. Under the postal worker's fleshy lips, shiny droplets dripped, and he started to snore.

Along the way, the car was popping like firecrackers as it cursed at the oxcarts.

The car was full of wind, overflowing and splashing, running wild on the vast plains, racing on the felt of tender green.

Poplars, willows, villages, fertile plains, sliding backward. Green, green, green, a vast sea. A flash of trembling, fiery peach blossoms, smoky pear blossoms, egg-yellow vegetable fields… sliding by. A bump, and delicate shadows fall over us… mottled cloth pieces, open to the wind, flutter and jump. Village girls wring their hands, laughing and talking, laughter echoes in the green… Clang! A bucket is lowered into a well. A hen, elegant and calm, retreats in surprise from the road into the wheat field. Piglets wag their ears, and waddle towards the pond. Disappeared. Poplars, willows, villages, fertile plains…

…The city gate had collapsed tiles, and on the wall was a large white character: "National Goods Gate." The journey naturally came to an end here.

Seeing A-Bao Off From the Golden Age (Continued) 212

— Zikai

Every time I go to Shanghai, I bring back some sweets to share with the children, adding to the family's happiness. A large part of the children's anticipation of my return lies in these "goodies." You have always been one of those who eagerly awaited these "goodies." You once competed with your siblings to see who would be the last to finish eating; you once collected the colorful gold and silver tinfoil and made them into gorgeous handicrafts, making your siblings envious. How could you now even think of hiding your own share and giving it all to your siblings? I saw you divide it evenly for them, expressing great joy, just like when you won the competition to be the last to finish eating. I couldn't help but lean on the window and laugh to myself. Because I remembered your childhood: ten years ago, you were a troublemaker in our family, crying several times a day for unmet demands, and getting beaten by your mother several times. You only ate the yolks of eggs, not the whites. If your mother accidentally put a piece of egg white in your rice bowl, you would scatter the rice grains and egg white all over the table, while shouting, "Want yolk! Want yolk!" You thought that anything good was called "yellow." So once when you wanted a small chair to play with, your mother gave you a small stool, but you shouted, "Want yellow! Want yellow!" You looked down on Ruan Ruan, who was two years old at the time and could barely move. When eating, you would save the bad stuff for Ruan Ruan; when telling stories, you would assign the unlucky roles to Ruan Ruan. When your mother refused to grant you a request, you would loudly ask: "Wrong Ruan Ruan? Wrong Ruan Ruan?" You meant that Ruan Ruan was no good and her requests could be denied; but A-Bao was an extremely important person, so how could her requests not be granted? The reason for the refusal must be that Ruan Ruan had been mistaken for A-Bao. So you would loudly remind your mother each time, insisting that she recognize A-Bao's true identity and grant all her requests. This troublemaker who only "wanted yellow" and specialized in bullying the weak, is now sacrificing his own happiness to increase the happiness of his siblings. Seeing this makes me feel both amused and sad. All your former ambitions and dreams have been declared a failure. You have begun to restrain your own demands, endure your own desires, and seek the happiness of others; you are about to leave your ego-centric golden age and begin to taste the bitterness of human love.

I remember one day last year, I had to leave home for a long journey for necessary business. In the past, whenever I had to go out, you would all be unhappy, trying to stop me or asking me to return early. Even earlier, I had to sneak out without you knowing. Later, when your brother couldn't find me, he would cry several times. When I returned, if you knew the date, you would often come to the door or halfway to meet me. The painting I made with the title "Papa Won't Come Back" was based on you and your brother waiting for me to return home. Because in the past ten years or so, I had considered you as the solace of my life, telling you stories, playing games, and eating snacks with you every night, making you all feel the warmth of family life. You couldn't do without a father, so you wouldn't let me leave home. On that day last year when I had to go out, your siblings still bid me farewell and asked me to return early. I thought you would do the same, and was about to ask you when I should come home and what things I should buy, but unexpectedly you advised me to leave early and return late, saying that you had all sorts of ways to distract your siblings from stopping me and waiting for me. It turned out that you had overheard me and your mother talking and knew that I needed to leave early and return late on this trip, and you had decided to share the hardships of life for me. I felt relieved on this trip, but I also felt sad. Because my family was about to lose a happy child of the golden age.

The above are all things of the past, but they are often imprinted in my mind, making it impossible for me to forget. Now, you are a middle school student, and soon you will leave the golden age and step into the world of adults. I feel that this journey is more important than getting married. An ancient poem about seeing a daughter off to be married says: "Raised by elders since childhood, two farewells cause endless weeping. This binds the heart, righteous journey hard to return." Your "righteous journey" out of the golden age is actually even harder to "return" than getting married, so how can I not "bind my heart"? Therefore, I am now recalling my feelings and writing this article to see you off. The place you are going to is the world depicted in this collection of my paintings. I am very worried about this trip of yours. It's like marrying you off from the side of loving parents to the house of an evil mother-in-law, just as the previous poem says: "Trained within the confines since childhood, serving the mother-in-law brings me worry." What kind of attitude to take when serving the mother-in-law, I find it difficult to decide for you. But I hope you will strive to love yourself and not bring me worry.

About ten years ago, I made a collection of books depicting your golden age. (Zikai's Book Collection). In its preface (To My Children) there were the following words: "My children! I yearn for your lives, more than once a day! I want to express it tactfully, so that you yourselves may know. Unfortunately, by the time you understand my words, you will no longer be the people who can make me yearn. What a sad thing this is! "But your golden age is limited, and reality will eventually be exposed. This is the situation I have experienced, and it is the situation that all adults have experienced. I have seen the heroes and good men among my childhood companions shrink, submit, compromise, and yield, to the point of becoming like sheep. I myself am the same. Later generations will view the present just as we view the past, and you will soon have to walk this path too!" The scene of writing these words is still vivid in my mind, and now you have indeed "understood my words," and you are indeed about to "walk this path"! Impermanence is swift, thinking of this again, how can I not "bind my heart"! (End)

Untitled 213

— Juan Shi

It rained all day again.

Sitting in the room, there's nothing to do except read, or else listen to the sound of the rain, approaching from afar and finally pouring down in torrents. When this sound winds its way into this lonely room, when it draws near me and makes me look up, the window becomes tightly entwined with a very melancholy, very bleak scene. Grey clouds, looking utterly bored, tightly cover everything, and large raindrops scatter randomly on the already dim glass. But what is especially desolate is the steamboat whistle in the rain, a sharp, mournful whistle, coming from the steamboat docked on the little river across the way, originally meant as a signal for departure, but unexpectedly bringing an uncontrollable sense of sorrow to some unrelated people. After one sound, another follows, and the dust of the rain continues to sprinkle on the windowpane. In the thin cold, I see two shivering sparrows flying into the sky, everything lacking the brightness of spring, the radiance of midday, and so people seem particularly melancholy.

The small room, when the dark clouds began to spread, had already lit the lamp. One side was still invaded by the faint light of the uncompletely retreated daylight, thus blending into a very dim but very charming scene. The silent furniture, at this time of day, should have been covered with the golden light of the sun, and the person sitting on it should also have a mood as sunny as the weather, smiling leisurely. But now, instead of sunlight, there is only lamplight, which gently strokes every corner of the room with a pair of charming fingers, soft, but also weak, coupled with the bookshelf full of books, the messy packages, the whitewashed walls, creating a very lingering mood.

In my hand is a play by Chekhov, and with tired eyes I capture the man's wisdom from between the lines. When he pours out everything that is hidden in his heart, I have a strange feeling of being lost. The book tells the story of a person whose youth has passed, and after spending his whole life in foolish efforts, some faint sparks suddenly ignite in his heart.

Thus, he makes desperate, presumptuous demands, and finally all his dreams vanish like bubbles. The strings of life, after experiencing reality, relax lazily. He thinks he still has to live on, so he uses numbness and boredom to pass the days that follow. Holding the heavy book, I imagine this middle-aged man spending another twenty or thirty years in that old garden, in that desolate house, and then dying without resistance. Some hot tears, like spring rain, swirl in my eyes.

People cannot have ideals, cannot have yearnings, those are just games for the idle. When you are young, you may have good dreams, round dreams like the spring moon. The person who is dreaming is always happy, cut off from everything outside, wandering in the illusory mirage, of course, this good dream can be extended for ten or twenty years, because for this pathetic creature called mankind, there should be a short period to enjoy this tragic grace. And so he lives like this, this illusion gradually leaves him, like a friend saying goodbye forever, perhaps gradually moving away, or perhaps suddenly disappearing without a trace, but it is all the same. And so this period ends for him, at first there should be struggling, but that is also so weak, pitiful struggling! Slowly he puts down his hands and waits quietly for fate to embed him in a stereotyped mold. Later he dies, his eyes, which have gazed upon many faces of life, close, he no longer struggles, he is quiet. At that time, if death has not rendered him unconscious, a feeling may arise in his heart, which may not be the same for everyone, but may not be very different either, and that is: "I have already lived, I never knew that life was so plain!"

Surrounding me, behind me, to my left and right, are all grey shadows of grey phantoms, all a pitiable, helpless, silent group. I can't bear it anymore. When will I be able to open the window and bathe in the golden sunshine? The raindrops just keep falling, falling, the raindrops flatten my hope.

This man has only the appearance of a gentleman, and can only frighten birds.

Rain (3) 214

— He Wei

Clouds and fog blocked his view and locked his heart. His thoughts seemed to float in mid-air, blown by the wind into scattered pieces, drifting and swaying, with no end in sight. He felt cold and hungry. The whole morning passed, the whole afternoon also passed, and night had already filled the entire earth, but his uncle and the others were still nowhere to be seen.

The doors of Juanzi's house were tightly closed, and had not been opened since his uncle went inside. The village was asleep in the wind and rain, with only the sounds of chickens and dogs barking. The rain kept falling, rustling, rustling, truly making one uncomfortable. When he saw the smoke rising from the rooftops of the village, gradually blending into the depths of the clouds and fog, Tianli really couldn't stay alone in the pavilion any longer. He looked at that house with its heavily locked doors, feeling both angry and hateful, wishing he could kick his way into the courtyard inside those high walls and, no matter what the old woman said, pick up Juanzi and leave.

He walked slowly along the ridge, sticking his head out from under the umbrella and looking ahead. Although the ridge was made of stones, it had fallen into disrepair over the years, and there were mud puddles everywhere, making it very difficult to walk. He remembered that when he was younger, he had walked this short ridge with Juanzi side by side. They carried the same umbrella, pressed close together. Sometimes she would walk very fast, snatching the umbrella and running forward, making him chase after her, getting soaked in the rain; sometimes she would walk very slowly, making him follow her as if she were a female character in an old opera with bound feet. Her temper was fickle, and she would often stop for no reason, as stiff as a frozen stone, and he would have to say many humble words before she would move again. One moment she would be singing, listening to her own singing, echoing in the valley; the next moment she would be in tears, watching her own tears mingle with the drizzle. So, even though it was only a short low ridge, the little girl's affection and sweetness were enough to savor.

"When will I be able to be together with Juanzi again?"

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Law Student Fraud Case 215

— Chui

Lawyers have the mission of safeguarding human rights, so when people's lives and property are unjustly violated, lawyers can request relief from the court according to the law. Therefore, their authority is so great, their responsibility is so important, and their status is so superior. Therefore, their knowledge of the law is naturally very well prepared. For example, for crimes such as forging documents and obtaining property by fraud, they must know exactly which article and section of the law to punish, as if reciting family treasures. Unexpectedly, recently, two outstanding law students have committed the act of jointly forging documents and defrauding money, trying to taste the flavor of stepping into the legal net in practice, which is truly astonishing.

According to reports, a law school graduate named Yuan Haiguang needed funds to apply for a lawyer's certificate from the Ministry of Justice. He discussed it with his classmate Jiang Yuanling, but they could not find a way. They used two Xinhua Bank checks in the name of the law school alumni association to fraudulently purchase a typewriter from the British-owned Wenyi Foreign Firm, mortgaged it for eighty-eight yuan, and divided the loot for their own use. This is truly an absurd idea, disgrace to intellectuals, and the ultimate misfortune for university students.

Judging from the facts, these two university students, having the ability to study and graduate from law school, are now on the verge of failure. How could they be unable to find even one or two hundred yuan for the lawyer's certificate fee? Even if they didn't have it themselves, they could borrow from slightly wealthier relatives and friends. Such a legitimate purpose would not necessarily be absolutely refused by relatives and friends. Even if there was no other way, they could only wait for an opportunity or think of other ways to generate income. Why were they so impatient as to commit this act of fraud? Furthermore, the motive for this incident was to apply for a lawyer's certificate. It is said that the Ministry of Justice requires more than two hundred yuan to apply for a lawyer's certificate. How could defrauding only eighty-odd yuan be of any help? Moreover, the eighty-odd yuan was divided for their own use, so the claim of applying for a lawyer's certificate is also questionable.

As for poverty, it is a common ailment of the people of the Republic of China. Without poverty, one cannot become a good citizen today. But one must be poor with integrity, poor with decisiveness, and must not let poverty shorten one's ambition, or act perversely. One must still actively struggle and continue to work hard in the direction of the road and social environment in order to find a way out. As for forging documents and obtaining property by fraud, these are clearly acts of throwing oneself into the legal net and destroying one's own character. As the saying goes, scattering dirt behind the door does not prevent the dawn from breaking. In the end, there will be a day when the truth comes out.

Just think, Jiang used the law school alumni association's check to fraudulently purchase a typewriter from the Wenyi Foreign Firm. Although the Wenyi Foreign Firm could be deceived at a certain time, the foreign firm would definitely have to collect the cash from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank. Since it was forged, the seal would naturally not match, and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank would definitely refuse to pay the cash. If the foreign firm could not collect the cash, it would naturally have to investigate the source. Jiang and Yuan would ultimately have no way to escape punishment. This kind of simple fact was right in front of them, yet the two students were completely unaware, and were still rejoicing that their plan had succeeded. It is truly laughable. Even middle school students would not do this, nor would they want to do this. Yet, unexpectedly, a university student, and a law school student at that, would commit such an act. I cannot help but feel sad for the future of university students.

Death 216

— Tuoren

A few years ago, this aging P County still preserved the form of thousands of years ago. Everything was old, with no new tricks. Modern civilization had no shadow here, and scientific progress had not invaded here to leave any traces. Everything that had already leaped forward in the world and in the cities, in this ancient city, still had not left a single spark. Only the permanently unchanged face remained here. People lived as if they were in the Middle Ages. Things and all phenomena still had the characteristics of the Middle Ages. Everything seemed to live in stagnant water.

However, since a highway was built through here a few years ago, this ancient city has also changed. From that highway came all sorts of fresh, new things that the people living in this city had never seen before. They were surprised and felt novel, as if everyone was watching with eyes that did not believe themselves everything they thought was strange, fresh, and unimaginable. They were also conjecturing in their fantasies how beautiful the outside world was. When the automobile, which the people in this aging city could not even imagine in their fantasies, passed through here for the first time on the highway, everyone felt a special strangeness. Children were surrounded in groups around the car, looking with surprised eyes. The old men were even sighing with each other. They all said:

"Heaven and earth are really changing. All sorts of new things will appear. A car like this that doesn't need oxen or horses, or even people, is something that even in dreams you couldn't dream of having. How much effort did Kongming use to build wooden horses and wooden carts? People now are really smarter than Kongming."

Gradually, the things outside were transported by the cars that they thought were surprising. Food, clothing, and utensils poured endlessly into this city that had not changed from thousands of years ago to the present. People's lives were also attracted by the new things from outside, and

New things replaced the old. The aging P County already had a bit of new life ignited. However, the destruction of old things gave them a terrible phantom. This city, which relied on handicraft industry to live a medieval life, was all heading for bankruptcy.

A few years ago, the things they still thought were fresh, the new era that they were vigorously praising, although washing away their aging hearts over the years, although developing to the point of replacing everything, they were instead terrified. Everything they had, the nourishment for their lives, was taken away by the cars running on the highway. So they felt sad, and started to hate the new things.

The terrible phantom, as dark as a forest at night, shrouded every corner of this already changed city, soaking into the depths of the hearts of everyone living here. All the thoughts of the initial admiration, surprise, hope, and joy were covered by the terrible phantom, and what now occupied their minds was exactly the opposite. What floated back into their minds was the revival of the already dead life, the reappearance of the aging city and old things. Yes, those were already thought to be unsatisfactory, but those were still good, those were still able to increase the flames of their lives compared to the new things now. So the children no longer surrounded and watched the strange monster running on the highway, and the old men were no longer so surprised. They were sighing again, this sigh was covered with a layer of grey. They said:

"The grace that the new things give us is death. All the fire of our lives has been extinguished."

Alas! Hurry and go.

Alley 217

— Yafei

Ten years ago, I used to live in this alley. I never thought I would revisit this old place. However, the alley before my eyes is no longer what it was ten years ago.

I remember when we lived here, the watchtower outside was still intact, and an old drifter lived underneath. Apart from our house, which stood tall and alone, several houses in the alley had already become dilapidated walls, and some courtyards had been turned into vegetable or fruit gardens. However, in the dilapidated mansion of an imperial censor across from our house, there still lived a watchman from this street, an old fellow from Shandong. He was already in his forties but still didn't have a wife. According to him, his father was the gatekeeper of this censor's mansion.

This magnificent censor's mansion, I imagined in those days, was very prominent. Not to mention anything else, just the watchtower was impressive enough. Such an antique building is probably rarely seen nowadays! The bottom of the alley was paved with whole fine sandstone slabs, and the section at the street entrance was paved with a "penny stone." In front of the censor's mansion, the courtyard was paved with Tian Tai stones arranged into a very delicate "flat promotion of three grades." A "carp leaping over the dragon gate" was built on the gate tower, and a pair of stone horses were placed on both sides of the gate, how solemn it was! I once heard people say that in the late Qing dynasty, civil officials had to dismount their sedan chairs when passing by here, and military officials had to dismount their horses, but after the establishment of the Republic of China, this kind of scene disappeared.

The alley was very wide, and an eight-person sedan chair could easily pass through.

In the past, the alley was originally called "Censor Alley." No one knows when the name "Slum Alley" came about. I think perhaps after the censor retired to the countryside, he didn't want to keep the name "Censor" and felt that the words "Slum Alley" were too pleasant and too elegant, so he wanted to call it that...

It seems that when I was a child, the censor's mansion wasn't as dilapidated as it is now. The magnolia tree in the back garden was where my sister An and I picked flowers and chased butterflies. That old Shandong fellow, everyone called him Old Shandong. Although he was in his forties, his childishness was no less than ours. When he was free, besides drinking, he would play with us.

Childhood, as soon as I think of my already gone, unrecoverable childhood, I feel sad, because my childhood was gray, just like now, with nothing worth savoring. It's just like a gray dream, quickly flying away in my life.

But the gray dream of childhood still retains some innocence, so it still feels somewhat lovely. But now, what about now? Even this only innocence is gone: all that's left of reality is a mass of gray life!

Ah! I want to mourn my lost childhood here.

Time blew through my life like a hurricane: it blew away my childhood, blew away my youth, blew away my lovely companion, blew away my dear sister An, blew away...

Because of Sister An's death, I returned to the slum alley I had left ten years ago with a burst of grief. Now, revisiting the old place, the new sorrows are even deeper, and I feel like my life is like a lonely boat without a rudder, drifting in the vast ocean, and the only light of the lighthouse has now been completely extinguished. Moved by the scene, I can't help but burst into tears!

The slum alley is still the slum alley of ten years ago, but the situation seems even more desolate and shabby than it was ten years ago. The magnolia tree in the censor's mansion has also been climbed and broken into a few bare branches. Even the old Shandong fellow, although still barely alive, is so old and feeble that he is no longer as strong as he used to be. His miserable life is naturally imaginable. When I talked to him about the past, his dry and wrinkled eyes became a little moist.

Night Crossing of Ganzhu Shoal 218

— Ai Tu

Carried by the transport ship with the wandering heart of a prodigal son, I floated like duckweed across the bay and through the raging waves—my mood was really like a bird without a rope, with strings of wounds given to me by the darkness of the world floating in my heart, as if every event had left an unforgettable shadow on me.

(Another wandering son has returned.—Perhaps mother is thinking this. However, mother would at least remember the last time, about two years ago in the summer, when I went home, I hadn't completely shed my childishness. Jumping and skipping, although it could be said that I had left my hometown and entered society, wandering everywhere. However, my economic ability at that time gave me quite a bit of happiness and full of joy, so when I returned, mother, poor mother, welcomed me with tears: "Son! Don't be so impetuous, listen to people's guidance, even if you don't study, you have to do something. Look, you're sixteen years old, in another two or three years you should be getting married! You've been smart since you were a child, you shouldn't go down the wrong path!" Yes, mother missed me so much. But what about now? How have I wandered? A sickly, haggard, melancholic face, a body broken by the hardships of the journey, everything has changed. Everything has changed, perhaps, this appearance of mine, this pale face, can only increase mother's infinite sadness and tears.)

On the ferry, I was thinking so melancholically about endless stories, the faces of some familiar brothers, friends, and relatives, the bright faces of smiling innocent little sisters, lovely innocent smiles, which had carved indelible dreamlike shadows on my childhood life.—Thinking, thinking, there really are endless poetic and terrible predicaments in the life of a wanderer. Sometimes I'm so happy that even a small thing feels strange and great, but sometimes I feel like everything is haunted by terrible black demons. At those times, I always curse that life is simply a difficult and painful road, full of thorns and bitterness,—that's right, although I am so young, I understand many things. Now, it can be said that I have returned with a heart full of melancholy and pain.

When the ship sailed from the raging sea into the inland river, it was the time when blood-red sunset filled the western mountains, making it impossible for me to stop the melancholic tide of my thoughts. At this time, I could go up to the deck of the ship and stare at the blue, darkening sky. The golden light reflected from the calm sea, the sounds floating out from the lush forests on the shore, and the dense reeds swaying gently in the evening sea breeze, were like a poor daughter stranded on a deserted island. Sad, (the evening sea is just like this, containing infinite sorrow!)

Following the turning rhythm of the clock, the transport ship kept rolling out silver-white waves towards both banks. At the same time, my head also rolled with the turning rhythm, like the waves of the sea—after all, it is only at dusk that one realizes the mood of wandering, like an unfathomable melancholic picture.

When the wind floating on the sea gradually carried a cool breath, a shadow came to tell me habitually again—night was coming, and the sea stone gate of Ganzhu Shoal had arrived. At the same time, I remember that not long after the ship crossed Ganzhu Shoal, I should fall asleep, letting the transport ship struggle with the darkness, carrying our tired bodies, and when the beautiful and clear dawn hung in the east, my hometown would appear before my eyes.

When the ship arrived at Ganzhu Shoal, apart from the dark shadows of the mountains and forests on both banks, which seemed to bewitch like ghosts and demons, and a few sparse stars in the sky, nothing could be heard or seen. At this time, I heard a huge wave even bigger than the waves of the sea—Ganzhu Shoal is a place of sea stone gates, with several large rocks standing on the seabed, which can capsize ships at any time—indeed, this is a very dangerous place.

However, passing through this place smoothly and alarmingly, I looked uneasily at the road home. (The night brings melancholy thoughts!)

Notes of a Weary Traveler 219

— Ji Tuan

"When a person gradually grows older and the experience of life gradually accumulates, he will be tired of running on the path paved with the sharp stones of emotion; then, let him be called the weary traveler on the path of affection."

Finally, one time, I boldly told her these terrible words that I had long kept secret. Then I quickly turned my head—I was afraid to see her frightened, disappointed, and intensely hurt face; but a string of low monologues still couldn't escape drifting past my ear: "What are you saying—you, you're still very young. You—"

Yes, maybe I really am still very young; but young people have two strong legs and a bold heart, and they are brave to gallop on the narrow path of emotion; but I have a withered heart of a weary traveler, and why do I carry so much of the sunset mood of middle age?

Then I thought: Even if I am young in her mouth, natural reality everywhere gives me the threat of sinking. Perhaps her words are just a kind of tranquilizer for me, while the threat of reality is a kind of warning? If that is really the case, then I would rather abandon her deceptive, embellished, and anesthetizing tranquilizer, and more gratefully accept the valuable warning given to me by the phenomenon of nature. Because what the former comforts me is a kind of deception; while the latter, even if it frightens me, is also a very precious truth.

Yes, it is no longer the age of youth; it is already a weary traveler tired of running on the narrow path of emotion!

Opening the many books deeply closed in my heart that record the travels and adventures in the wilderness of feelings, those wheat-like records can no longer make people yearn for them; young people are curious and adventurous, holding a renewed and exciting heart, carrying a walking stick, carrying a food bag, and sometimes, perhaps carrying a compass and a small travel guide, and then they go alone to the wilderness of feelings in the human world. There are poetic clouds and flowers there, and there are also black skies before thunderstorms. Patiently crossing the steps of the journey, the times are also moving forward step by step; barren mountains and deep pits have been passed, and small streams and orchards have also been passed: the birds of spring are happy, and the trees of summer also have countless vitality, but now it is already autumn. The wilderness of feelings is not suitable for autumn travel, look at the boundless gray-yellow desert and the earthen mounds without water and grass.

So what is written in the traveler's travelogue are all terrible poems like nightmares, the traveler's courage is gone, and the traveler's youthful curiosity is exhausted. Putting down the walking stick and luggage, what he needs is no longer the search for wonders, but only ordinary, with no climaxes and no lows, as quiet as an old man in the countryside resting—sitting quietly in the sun to smoke a pipe and take a breath. The traveler is no longer young, nor does he have youthful curiosity: the traveler is tired!

It is no longer worth reminiscing and feeling sad. The wilderness of emotion will never be as magical as a garden. People live, and people also run on the small path of affection paved with sharp stones. And now, people are tired from constant fatigue, people need to find a path to return, people need to rest!

Let everything that has passed pass, and let everything that is to come come! In short, the journey back from running on the small path of emotion is already as tired as an old ox. Don't ask me about those nightmarish travelogues, and don't pull me back onto the rugged road of emotion—take a careful look at the weary face of the dusty traveler.

Shenbao Architectural Weekly

Design of Public Memorial Buildings 228

— Xiao Ang

In recent years, the construction of public memorials has become a trend in various parts of our country. However, the characteristics and spirit of these memorial buildings must be expressed through architectural skills. Therefore, their design aspect is very worthy of study. Generally, the design of a building must meet the following four principles. I will now elaborate on the design of public memorial buildings based on these four principles.

(1) Utility Generally, public memorial buildings, such as Zhongshan Memorial Hall, Martyrs' Memorial Tower, and Revolutionary Martyrs' Shrine, all have their special purposes and values. Therefore, the choice of location and style is a very important issue. If the selection is poor, its utility will be lost. Memorial buildings should be built in places with pleasant scenery and convenient transportation. The terrain should be high all around, and it is advisable to leave plenty of open space so that they can be seen from all directions. As for the style, many architects say that the architecture of Greece and Rome is very majestic and exquisite, and is most suitable for memorials. I think Chinese-style architecture is also very good. If you go to Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in Nanjing and Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall in Guangzhou, you will feel that the architecture is magnificent, the project is vast, and the terrain is suitable, which is awe-inspiring. If you go to the Dunhuang Grottoes and Baima Temples, you will think of the prosperity of the Tang Dynasty's cultural relics and the majesty of the empire. These are all inherent Chinese architectural styles, but they do not lose their utility, and they are no less than Western architecture. Why don't architects glorify the inherent Chinese architectural style?

(2) Solidity Public memorial buildings must be particularly solid, lasting for thousands of years without damage, able to withstand the pressure of wind and snow, the ravages of people, the erosion of water and humidity, and the burning of fire. Therefore, the choice of building materials is also very important. Granite is the most durable material in the stone category. Marble is more expensive, but it is much more beautiful. Reinforced concrete is also very good. When it comes to solidity, it is second only to granite, but because it is cheaper, it is also widely used. Memorial buildings made of wood and copper and iron are the least common.

(3) Aesthetics In addition to utility and solidity, what can fully express the spirit of the building is to start from the aesthetic aspect. The form of the building and the color of the materials should be uniform to avoid being scattered. The structure should be varied so that it does not look stagnant. All buildings should be symmetrical to show that solemn atmosphere. The style should be unique to show seclusion and elegance. These are all to increase the aesthetics and attract people.

(4) Economy At this time of national crisis and increased pain, all public buildings may be simpler and more economical in order to save money.

Humble Opinions on Architectural "Methods" and "Calculations" 229

— Ouyang Gu

Regarding the records of architectural engineering "methods" in China, the Ministry of Works and the inner court of the Qing Dynasty have clearly promulgated them, and many craftsmen have followed them as procedures. However, the so-called "methods" in engineering are generally oral work that is passed on to apprentices by carpenters, and it is very difficult to say under the pen and ink. Therefore, the methods and rules promulgated at that time were actually algorithms rather than methods. Methods need to explain how to start, how to saw, how to plane, how to install... In short, explain "how to do", these are all living things. "Calculations" need to explain the quantitative principles of the structural part functions, including the relationship of all sizes and positions. For example, the Pythagorean theorem for the base of the wall base built by the bricklayers is originally simple plane geometry. If it is written out in words and added with some unclear and unsavory songs, wouldn't it be confusing instead? Our purpose is in architecture, not in mathematics, but we also need a concise and reformed "calculation" method. For example, the most accurate method for finding the circumference of a circle is "multiply the diameter by three point one four one six", but the average plasterer and carpenter use the "three three plus it" algorithm when calculating the circumference, which is too far apart. This kind of error is still superficial. If the number is large, "a hair's breadth error can lead to a thousand miles' loss", that would be terrible.

The changes in architecture are infinite. Whether it is an engineer or a plasterer and carpenter, they must understand the secret of extrapolating from one example. It is impossible to simply enlarge or reduce a certain building by one point or one inch. Because the length, width and height of each part of each building are independent and absolute, and cannot be used as a basis or ratio. Therefore, the "calculation" occupies a very important position in construction, and it must be accurate, and this is the reason.

Now, people who study architecture from a modern perspective pay attention to the important points, mostly in art and engineering, and ignore the two methods that our country originally had, "model room" and "calculation room". Here, it is also necessary to explain the special responsibilities of these two methods. The model room is similar to modern architects, and the main duty is design. The duty of the "calculation room" is more like the assistant civil engineer in modern times, who specializes in managing assistants who calculate materials. This algorithm also has many places that incidentally explain the "sample" aspect. Now, if we can also deduce the rules of the "sample" from the method of calculation, that would be a gratifying harvest.

Regarding the definitions and explanations of various parts of the building, this journal publishes "Architectural Jargon" in each issue, and its benefits are also great. It can make people who do not have a proper understanding of Chinese architecture not be very unfamiliar when they see these many strange nouns. In short, the creation of architecture is like the creation of all arts, and should not be restricted by all aspects. Those rigid "calculations" and armchair "methods" are like setting traps to destroy or bind the creativity of young architects, and at the same time, we must pay attention to "reviewing the old and knowing the new", thereby expanding knowledge and enabling a whole understanding of the architectural world, so as to open a new era in the history of Chinese architecture.

Past and Present Views of Architecture 230

— Xian Zhi

The development of architecture is mostly based on the prosperity of the city. In the past, architecture was developed on a plane. Today, most of it is pushed upwards, because the ground of the city is limited, and the development of buildings is infinite. If the city becomes more and more prosperous, then tall buildings will continue to grow taller. However, this kind of tallest building must be competent by experienced architectural experts, because not only the design must be precise, but also the smallest space must be used to create useful houses, and the latest and most economical equipment must be used. As for the appearance, we must also pay attention to the aesthetics. As shown in the picture, the building of a certain company in Seattle is one of the major buildings designed by architectural expert Mr. Klamon in the United States. The other buildings, such as the University of Washington and the Bank of California in the United States, were all designed by him. Mr. Klamon has accumulated thirty years of experience and built buildings worth more than tens of millions of US dollars. He has now come to Shanghai from the United States to cooperate with Mr. Peter, an engineer from the World Industrial Company. In the future, the buildings in this city, designed by the two gentlemen, will definitely have a new and perfect development. The address of the World Industrial Company is No. 668 Sichuan Road, telephone number 11778.
